Legislative capital of South Africa

| Coordinates: [33°55′31″S 18°25′26″E﻿ / ﻿33.92528°S 18.42389°E﻿ / -33.92528; 18.42389](https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Cape_Town&params=33_55_31_S_18_25_26_E_region:ZA-WC_type:city) ||

**Cape Town** ^[\[a\]](#cite_note-13)^ is the [legislative](/wiki/Legislature "Legislature") [capital](/wiki/Capital_city "Capital city") of [South Africa](/wiki/South_Africa "South Africa"). It is the country's oldest city and the seat of the [Parliament of South Africa](/wiki/Parliament_of_South_Africa "Parliament of South Africa").^[\[13\]](#cite_note-14)^ Cape Town is the country's second-largest city, after [Johannesburg](/wiki/Johannesburg "Johannesburg"), and the largest in the [Western Cape](/wiki/Western_Cape "Western Cape").^[\[14\]](#cite_note-15)^ The city is part of the [City of Cape Town](/wiki/City_of_Cape_Town "City of Cape Town") [metropolitan municipality](/wiki/Metropolitan_municipality_(South_Africa) "Metropolitan municipality (South Africa)").{#cite_ref-15}

The city is known for [its harbour](/wiki/Port_of_Cape_Town "Port of Cape Town"), its natural setting in the [Cape Floristic Region](/wiki/Cape_Floristic_Region "Cape Floristic Region"), and for landmarks such as [Table Mountain](/wiki/Table_Mountain "Table Mountain") and [Cape Point](/wiki/Cape_Point "Cape Point"). In 2014, Cape Town was named the best place in the world to visit by *[The New York Times](/wiki/The_New_York_Times "The New York Times")* ,^[\[15\]](#cite_note-16)^ and was similarly ranked number one by *[The Daily Telegraph](/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph "The Daily Telegraph")* in both 2016 and 2023.^[\[16\]](#cite_note-17)^^[\[17\]](#cite_note-18)^{#cite_ref-18}

Located on the shore of [Table Bay](/wiki/Table_Bay "Table Bay"), the City Bowl area of Cape Town is [the oldest urban area in the Western Cape](/wiki/History_of_Cape_Town "History of Cape Town"), with a significant cultural heritage. It was founded by the [Dutch East India Company](/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company "Dutch East India Company") (VOC) as a supply station for Dutch ships sailing to [East Africa](/wiki/East_Africa "East Africa"), [India](/wiki/India "India"), and the [Far East](/wiki/Far_East "Far East"). [Jan van Riebeeck](/wiki/Jan_van_Riebeeck "Jan van Riebeeck")'s arrival on 6 April 1652 established the [VOC Cape Colony](/wiki/Dutch_Cape_Colony "Dutch Cape Colony"), the first permanent European settlement in South Africa.

Cape Town outgrew its original purpose as the first European outpost at the [Castle of Good Hope](/wiki/Castle_of_Good_Hope "Castle of Good Hope"), becoming the economic and cultural hub of the [Cape Colony](/wiki/Cape_Colony "Cape Colony"). Until the [Witwatersrand Gold Rush](/wiki/Witwatersrand_Gold_Rush "Witwatersrand Gold Rush") and the development of Johannesburg, Cape Town was the largest city in southern Africa.

The metropolitan area has a long coastline on the [Atlantic Ocean](/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean "Atlantic Ocean"), which includes False Bay, and extends to the [Hottentots Holland mountains](/wiki/Hottentots_Holland_Mountains "Hottentots Holland Mountains") to the east. The [Table Mountain National Park](/wiki/Table_Mountain_National_Park "Table Mountain National Park") is within the city boundaries and there are several other nature reserves and marine-protected areas within, and adjacent to, the city, protecting the diverse terrestrial and marine natural environment.  

History {#History}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: History")\]  
Main articles: [History of Cape Town](/wiki/History_of_Cape_Town "History of Cape Town") and [Timeline of Cape Town](/wiki/Timeline_of_Cape_Town "Timeline of Cape Town")

| External videos ||
|---|---|
| ![video icon](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_kaboodle.svg.png) ["Khoisan group renames the cape"](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=h1stIhiV5L0)--- 2012 news report by [Eyewitness News](/wiki/Eyewitness_News_(South_Africa) "Eyewitness News (South Africa)") on the official Khoekhoe naming of Cape Town as "ǁHuiǃgaeb" and how it is pronounced ||

### Early period {#Early_period}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: Early period")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/F._Benda-The_planting_of_cross_by_Bartholomew_Dias_in_1488-0681_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-F._Benda-The_planting_of_cross_by_Bartholomew_Dias_in_1488-0681_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:F._Benda-The_planting_of_cross_by_Bartholomew_Dias_in_1488-0681_(cropped).jpg) Portuguese explorer [Bartolomeu Dias](/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias "Bartolomeu Dias") planting the cross at [Cape Point](/wiki/Cape_Point "Cape Point"), 1488.

The earliest known remnants of human occupation in the region were found at Peers Cave in [Fish Hoek](/wiki/Fish_Hoek "Fish Hoek") and have been dated to between 15,000 and 12,000 years old.^[\[18\]](#cite_note-19)^^\[*[better source needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS "Wikipedia:NOTRS")*\]^{#cite_ref-19}

[Bartolomeu Dias](/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias "Bartolomeu Dias"), the first European to reach the area, arrived in 1488 and named it "Cape of Storms" (*Cabo das Tormentas*). It was later renamed by [John II of Portugal](/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal "John II of Portugal") as "[Cape of Good Hope](/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope "Cape of Good Hope")" (*Cabo da Boa Esperança*) because of the great optimism engendered by the opening of a sea route to the [Indian subcontinent](/wiki/Indian_subcontinent "Indian subcontinent") and [East Indies](/wiki/East_Indies "East Indies").

In 1497, Portuguese explorer [Vasco da Gama](/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama "Vasco da Gama") recorded a sighting of the Cape of Good Hope.

In 1510, at the [Battle of Salt River](/wiki/Battle_of_Salt_River "Battle of Salt River"), the Portuguese admiral [Francisco de Almeida](/wiki/Francisco_de_Almeida "Francisco de Almeida") and sixty-four of his men were killed and his party was defeated^[\[19\]](#cite_note-20)^ by the "Goringhaiqua" in Dutch approximate spelling) using cattle that were specially trained to respond to whistles and shouts.^[\[20\]](#cite_note-21)^ The Gorinaiqua were one of the [Khoikhoi](/wiki/Khoikhoi "Khoikhoi") clans who inhabited the area.{#cite_ref-21}

In the late 16th century French, Danish, Dutch, and English, but mainly Portuguese, ships regularly continued to stop over in Table Bay en route to the Indies. They traded tobacco, copper, and iron with the [Khoikhoi](/wiki/Khoikhoi_language "Khoikhoi language") clans of the region in exchange for fresh meat and other essential traveling provisions.  

### Dutch period {#Dutch_period}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Dutch period")\]  
Dutch period  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Charles_Bell_-_Jan_van_Riebeeck_se_aankoms_aan_die_Kaap.jpg/220px-Charles_Bell_-_Jan_van_Riebeeck_se_aankoms_aan_die_Kaap.jpg)](/wiki/File:Charles_Bell_-_Jan_van_Riebeeck_se_aankoms_aan_die_Kaap.jpg)  
[Jan van Riebeeck](/wiki/Jan_van_Riebeeck "Jan van Riebeeck") and Dutch colonists arriving in [Table Bay](/wiki/Table_Bay "Table Bay") in 1652.  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Cape_Town_in_1800.jpg/220px-Cape_Town_in_1800.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cape_Town_in_1800.jpg)  
A diorama of Cape Town as it would have appeared in 1800 at the end of Dutch rule by the VOC.  
See also: [Dutch Cape Colony](/wiki/Dutch_Cape_Colony "Dutch Cape Colony")

In 1652, [Jan van Riebeeck](/wiki/Jan_van_Riebeeck "Jan van Riebeeck") and other employees of the [United East India Company](/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company "Dutch East India Company") ([Dutch](/wiki/Dutch_language "Dutch language"): *Verenigde Oost-indische Compagnie* , VOC) were sent to the Cape Colony to establish a way-station for ships travelling to the [Dutch East Indies](/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies "Dutch East Indies"), and the [Fort de Goede Hoop](/wiki/Fort_de_Goede_Hoop "Fort de Goede Hoop") (later replaced by the [Castle of Good Hope](/wiki/Castle_of_Good_Hope "Castle of Good Hope")). The settlement grew slowly during this period, as it was hard to find adequate labour. This labour shortage prompted the local authorities to import enslaved people from [Indonesia](/wiki/Indonesia "Indonesia") and [Madagascar](/wiki/Madagascar "Madagascar"). Many of these people are ancestors of modern-day [Cape Coloured](/wiki/Cape_Coloureds "Cape Coloureds") and [Cape Malay](/wiki/Cape_Malays "Cape Malays") communities.^[\[21\]](#cite_note-22)^^[\[22\]](#cite_note-23)^{#cite_ref-23}

Under Van Riebeeck and his successors, as VOC commanders and later governors at the Cape, a wide range of agricultural plants were introduced to the Cape. Some of these, including grapes, cereals, ground nuts, potatoes, apples and citrus, had a large and lasting influence on the societies and economies of the region.^[\[23\]](#cite_note-24)^{#cite_ref-24}  

### British period {#British_period}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=4 "Edit section: British period")\]  
See also: [Cape Colony](/wiki/Cape_Colony "Cape Colony")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Adderley_Street%2C_Cape_Town%2C_looking_NE_-_ca._1897.jpg/220px-Adderley_Street%2C_Cape_Town%2C_looking_NE_-_ca._1897.jpg)](/wiki/File:Adderley_Street,_Cape_Town,_looking_NE_-_ca._1897.jpg) [Adderley Street](/wiki/Adderley_Street "Adderley Street") in 1897 was an important commercial hub in Cape Town at a time when the city was the most important centre of economic activity in the Southern Africa region.

With the [Dutch Republic](/wiki/Dutch_Republic "Dutch Republic") being transformed into [Revolutionary France](/wiki/First_French_Republic "First French Republic")'s vassal [Batavian Republic](/wiki/Batavian_Republic "Batavian Republic"), Great Britain moved to take control of Dutch colonies, including the colonial possessions of the VOC.

Britain [captured Cape Town in 1795](/wiki/Invasion_of_the_Cape_Colony "Invasion of the Cape Colony"), but it was returned to the Dutch by treaty in 1803. British forces occupied the Cape again in 1806 following the [Battle of Blaauwberg](/wiki/Battle_of_Blaauwberg "Battle of Blaauwberg") when the Batavian Republic allied with Britain's rival, France, during the [Napoleonic Wars](/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars "Napoleonic Wars"). Following the conclusion of the war Cape Town was permanently ceded to the United Kingdom in the [Anglo-Dutch Treaty of 1814](/wiki/Anglo-Dutch_Treaty_of_1814 "Anglo-Dutch Treaty of 1814").

The city became the capital of the newly formed [Cape Colony](/wiki/British_Cape_Colony "British Cape Colony"), whose territory expanded very substantially through the 1800s, partially as a result of [numerous wars](/wiki/Xhosa_Wars "Xhosa Wars") with the [amaXhosa](/wiki/Xhosa_people "Xhosa people") on the colony's eastern frontier. In 1833 slavery was [abolished in the colony](/wiki/Slavery_in_South_Africa#Abolition "Slavery in South Africa") freeing over 5500 slaves in the city, almost a third of the city's population at the time.^[\[24\]](#cite_note-Martin_1836_113-25)^ The [Convict Crisis](/wiki/Convict_crisis "Convict crisis") of 1849, marked by substantial civil upheaval, bolstered the push for self-governance in the Cape.^[\[25\]](#cite_note-:7-26)^^[\[26\]](#cite_note-:8-27)^ With expansion came calls for greater independence from the UK, with the Cape attaining [its own parliament](/wiki/Parliament_of_the_Cape_of_Good_Hope "Parliament of the Cape of Good Hope") (1854) and a locally accountable Prime Minister (1872). Suffrage was established according to the non-racial [Cape Qualified Franchise](/wiki/Cape_Qualified_Franchise "Cape Qualified Franchise").^[\[27\]](#cite_note-28)^^[\[28\]](#cite_note-29)^{#cite_ref-29}

During the 1850s and 1860s, additional plant species were introduced from Australia by the British authorities. Notably [rooikrans](/wiki/Acacia_cyclops "Acacia cyclops") was introduced to stabilise the sand of the [Cape Flats](/wiki/Cape_Flats "Cape Flats") to allow for a road connecting the peninsula with the rest of the African continent^[\[29\]](#cite_note-30)^ and [eucalyptus](/wiki/Eucalyptus "Eucalyptus") was used to drain marshes.^[\[30\]](#cite_note-31)^{#cite_ref-31}

In 1859 the first railway line was built by the [Cape Government Railways](/wiki/Cape_Government_Railways "Cape Government Railways") and a system of railways rapidly expanded in the 1870s. The discovery of diamonds in [Griqualand West](/wiki/Griqualand_West "Griqualand West") in 1867, and the [Witwatersrand Gold Rush](/wiki/Witwatersrand_Gold_Rush "Witwatersrand Gold Rush") in 1886, prompted a flood of immigration into South Africa.^[\[31\]](#cite_note-32)^ In 1895 the city's first public power station, the [Graaff Electric Lighting Works](/wiki/Graaff_Electric_Lighting_Works "Graaff Electric Lighting Works"), was opened.{#cite_ref-32}

Conflicts between the [Boer republics](/wiki/Boer_Republics "Boer Republics") in the interior and the British colonial government resulted in the [Second Boer War](/wiki/Second_Boer_War "Second Boer War") of 1899--1902. Britain's victory in this war led to the formation of a united South Africa. From 1891 to 1901, the city's population more than doubled from 67,000 to 171,000.^[\[32\]](#cite_note-C1875-33)^{#cite_ref-C1875_33-0}

As the 19th century came to an end, the economic and political dominance of Cape Town in the Southern Africa region during the 19th century started to give way to the dominance of Johannesburg and Pretoria in the 20th century.^[\[33\]](#cite_note-AMad-34)^{#cite_ref-AMad_34-0}  

### South African period {#South_African_period}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=5 "Edit section: South African period")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Cape_Town_foreshore_1946.jpg/220px-Cape_Town_foreshore_1946.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cape_Town_foreshore_1946.jpg) An aerial photograph of the newly completed [Cape Town foreshore](/wiki/Foreshore,_Cape_Town "Foreshore, Cape Town") in 1945. Visible in this photograph as the large area of empty land between the City Centre and the newly constructed harbour out of reclaimed land from [Table Bay](/wiki/Table_Bay "Table Bay").^[\[34\]](#cite_note-sahris_sahra_org_za-35)^

In 1910, Britain established the [Union of South Africa](/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa "Union of South Africa"), which unified the Cape Colony with the two defeated Boer Republics and the British [colony of Natal](/wiki/Colony_of_Natal "Colony of Natal"). Cape Town became the legislative capital of the Union, and later of the [Republic of South Africa](/wiki/Republic_of_South_Africa "Republic of South Africa").

By the time of the [1936 census](/wiki/South_African_National_Census_of_1936 "South African National Census of 1936"), Johannesburg had overtaken Cape Town as the largest city in the country.

In 1945 the expansion of the [Cape Town foreshore](/wiki/Foreshore,_Cape_Town "Foreshore, Cape Town") was completed adding an additional 194 ha (480 acres) to the [City Bowl](/wiki/City_Bowl "City Bowl") area to the city centre.^[\[34\]](#cite_note-sahris_sahra_org_za-35)^{#cite_ref-sahris_sahra_org_za_35-1}  

#### Apartheid era {#Apartheid_era}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=6 "Edit section: Apartheid era")\]

Prior to the mid-twentieth century, Cape Town was one of the most racially integrated cities in South Africa.^[\[35\]](#cite_note-36)^^[\[36\]](#cite_note-37)^ In the [1948 national elections](/wiki/1948_South_African_general_election "1948 South African general election"), the [National Party](/wiki/National_Party_(South_Africa) "National Party (South Africa)") won on a platform of *[apartheid](/wiki/Apartheid "Apartheid")* (racial segregation) under the slogan of "[swart gevaar](/wiki/Swart_gevaar "Swart gevaar")" (Afrikaans for "black danger"). This led to the erosion and eventual abolition of the [Cape's multiracial franchise](/wiki/Cape_Qualified_Franchise "Cape Qualified Franchise").{#cite_ref-37}

In 1950, the apartheid government first introduced the [Group Areas Act](/wiki/Group_Areas_Act "Group Areas Act"), which classified and segregated urban areas according to race. Formerly multi-racial suburbs of Cape Town were either purged of residents deemed unlawful by apartheid legislation, or demolished. The most infamous example of this in Cape Town was the suburb of [District Six](/wiki/District_Six,_Cape_Town "District Six, Cape Town"). After it was declared a whites-only area in 1965, all housing there was demolished and over 60,000 residents were forcibly removed.^[\[37\]](#cite_note-38)^ Many of these residents were relocated to the [Cape Flats](/wiki/Cape_Flats "Cape Flats").{#cite_ref-38}

The earliest of the Cape Flats forced removals saw the expulsion of Black South Africans to the [Langa](/wiki/Langa,_Western_Cape "Langa, Western Cape"), Cape Town's first and oldest township, in line with the 1923 [Native Urban Areas Act](/wiki/Natives_Urban_Areas_Act "Natives Urban Areas Act").

Under apartheid, the Cape was considered a "[Coloured](/wiki/Coloured "Coloured") labour preference area", to the exclusion of "[Bantus](/wiki/Bantu-speaking_peoples_of_South_Africa "Bantu-speaking peoples of South Africa")", i.e. Black Africans. The implementation of this policy was widely opposed by trade unions, civil society and opposition parties. It is notable that this policy was not advocated for by any Coloured political group, and its implementation was a unilateral decision by the apartheid government.^[\[38\]](#cite_note-39)^ During the student-led [Soweto Uprising](/wiki/Soweto_uprising "Soweto uprising") of June 1976, school students from [Langa](/wiki/Langa,_Western_Cape "Langa, Western Cape"), [Gugulethu](/wiki/Gugulethu "Gugulethu") and [Nyanga](/wiki/Nyanga,_Western_Cape "Nyanga, Western Cape") in Cape Town reacted to the news of the protests against Bantu Education by organising gatherings and marches of their own. A number of school buildings were burnt down and the protest action was met with forceful resistance from the police.^[\[39\]](#cite_note-40)^^[\[40\]](#cite_note-41)^{#cite_ref-41}

Cape Town has been home to many leaders of the [anti-apartheid movement](/wiki/Internal_resistance_to_apartheid "Internal resistance to apartheid"). In [Table Bay](/wiki/Table_Bay "Table Bay"), 10 km (6 mi) from the city is [Robben Island](/wiki/Robben_Island "Robben Island"). This [penitentiary island](/wiki/Maximum_Security_Prison,_Robben_Island "Maximum Security Prison, Robben Island") was the site of a maximum security prison where many famous apartheird-era political prisoners served long prison sentences. Famous prisoners include activist, lawyer and future president [Nelson Mandela](/wiki/Nelson_Mandela "Nelson Mandela") who served 18 of his 27 years of imprisonment on the island, as well as two other future presidents, [Kgalema Motlanthe](/wiki/Kgalema_Motlanthe "Kgalema Motlanthe") and [Jacob Zuma](/wiki/Jacob_Zuma "Jacob Zuma").^[\[41\]](#cite_note-42)^{#cite_ref-42}

In one of the most famous moments marking the end of apartheid, Nelson Mandela made his first public speech since his imprisonment, from the balcony of [Cape Town City Hall](/wiki/Cape_Town_City_Hall "Cape Town City Hall"), hours after being released on 11 February 1990. His speech heralded the beginning of a new era for the country. The [first democratic election](/wiki/South_African_general_election,_1994 "South African general election, 1994"), was held four years later, on 27 April 1994.^[\[42\]](#cite_note-43)^^[\[43\]](#cite_note-44)^^[\[44\]](#cite_note-45)^{#cite_ref-45}

[Nobel Square](/wiki/Nobel_Square "Nobel Square") in the [Victoria \& Alfred Waterfront](/wiki/Victoria_%26_Alfred_Waterfront "Victoria & Alfred Waterfront") features statues of South Africa's four [Nobel Peace Prize](/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize "Nobel Peace Prize") winners: [Albert Luthuli](/wiki/Albert_Luthuli "Albert Luthuli"), [Desmond Tutu](/wiki/Desmond_Tutu "Desmond Tutu"), [F. W. de Klerk](/wiki/F._W._de_Klerk "F. W. de Klerk") and [Nelson Mandela](/wiki/Nelson_Mandela "Nelson Mandela").^\[*[relevant?](/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Stay_on_topic "Wikipedia:Writing better articles") -- [discuss](/wiki/Talk:Cape_Town#Is_this_relevant_to_the_history_section? "Talk:Cape Town")*\]^  

#### Post-apartheid era {#Post-apartheid_era}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=7 "Edit section: Post-apartheid era")\]

Cape Town has undergone significant changes in the years since Apartheid. Cape Town has experienced economic growth and development in the post-apartheid era. The city has become a major economic hub in South Africa, attracting international investment and tourism. The [Democratic Alliance](/wiki/Democratic_Alliance_(South_Africa) "Democratic Alliance (South Africa)") (DA), a [liberal](/wiki/Liberalism "Liberalism") political party which came to power in Cape Town in 2006, has been credited with improving bureaucratic efficiency, public safety and fostering economic development.^[\[45\]](#cite_note-:0-46)^^[\[46\]](#cite_note-:1-47)^{#cite_ref-:1_47-0}

Opinion polls show that South Africans see it as the best governed province and city in the country.^[\[47\]](#cite_note-48)^^[\[48\]](#cite_note-49)^ Of South Africa's 257 municipalities, only 38 received a clean financial audit in 2022 from the [Auditor-General](/wiki/Auditor-General_(South_Africa) "Auditor-General (South Africa)"). Of those, 21 were in the Western Cape.^[\[45\]](#cite_note-:0-46)^ The city's economy has diversified, with growth in sectors such as finance, real estate, and tourism. The establishment of the City Centre Improvement District (CCID) has been particularly successful in revitalizing the city center, bringing businesses and people back into the area. This initiative has transformed public spaces such as [Greenmarket Square](/wiki/Greenmarket_Square "Greenmarket Square"), [Company's Garden](/wiki/Company%27s_Garden "Company's Garden"), and St George's Mall, attracting both locals and tourists.^[\[49\]](#cite_note-50)^{#cite_ref-50}

In 2014, Cape Town was named [World Design Capital](/wiki/World_Design_Capital "World Design Capital") of the Year.^[\[50\]](#cite_note-51)^ Cape Town was voted the best tourist destination in Africa at the 2023 World Travel Awards in [Dubai](/wiki/Dubai "Dubai") and continues to be the most important tourist destination in the country.^[\[51\]](#cite_note-52)^^[\[52\]](#cite_note-53)^ Cape Town has been named the best travel city in the world every year since 2013 in the [Telegraph](/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph "The Daily Telegraph") Travel Awards.^[\[53\]](#cite_note-54)^^[\[54\]](#cite_note-55)^{#cite_ref-55}

The legacy of apartheid's spatial planning is still evident, with significant disparities between affluent areas and impoverished [townships](/wiki/Township "Township").^[\[55\]](#cite_note-:2-56)^ 60% of the city's population live in townships and informal settlements far from the city centre.^[\[56\]](#cite_note-57)^ The legacy of Apartheid means Cape Town remains one of the most racially segregated cities in South Africa.^[\[57\]](#cite_note-58)^ Many Black South Africans continue to live in informal settlements with limited access to basic services such as healthcare, education, and sanitation.^[\[55\]](#cite_note-:2-56)^^[\[58\]](#cite_note-:3-59)^ The unemployment rate remains high at 23% (though nearly 10 points lower than the nationwide average), particularly among historically disadvantaged groups, and economic opportunities are unevenly distributed.^[\[46\]](#cite_note-:1-47)^{#cite_ref-:1_47-1}

Cape Town faced a [severe water shortage](/wiki/Cape_Town_water_crisis "Cape Town water crisis") from 2015 to 2018.^[\[59\]](#cite_note-60)^ According to [Oxfam](/wiki/Oxfam "Oxfam"), "in the face of an imminent water shortage, the city of Cape Town in South Africa successfully reduced its water use by more than half in three years, cutting it from 1.2bn litres per day in February 2015 to 516m litres per day in 2018."^[\[60\]](#cite_note-61)^{#cite_ref-61}

In 2021 Cape Town also experienced a [violent turf war](/wiki/2021_Cape_Town_taxi_conflict "2021 Cape Town taxi conflict") between [rival mini-bus taxi firms](/wiki/Taxi_wars_in_South_Africa "Taxi wars in South Africa") which led to the deaths of 83 people. Two years later [a strike by the mini-bus taxi firms](/wiki/2023_Cape_Town_taxi_strike "2023 Cape Town taxi strike") resulted in 5 deaths.

Since the 2010s, Cape Town and the wider Western Cape province have seen the rise of a small [secessionist movement](/wiki/Cape_Independence "Cape Independence").^[\[61\]](#cite_note-62)^ Support for parties "which have formally adopted Cape independence" was around 5% in the [2021 municipal elections](/wiki/2021_South_African_municipal_elections "2021 South African municipal elections").^[\[62\]](#cite_note-63)^{#cite_ref-63}  

Geography and the natural environment {#Geography_and_the_natural_environment}
------------------------------------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=8 "Edit section: Geography and the natural environment")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/The_Mother_City_-_South_Africa_%282417714757%29.jpg/220px-The_Mother_City_-_South_Africa_%282417714757%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_Mother_City_-_South_Africa_(2417714757).jpg) [Devil's Peak](/wiki/Devil%27s_Peak_(Cape_Town) "Devil's Peak (Cape Town)"), [Table Mountain](/wiki/Table_Mountain "Table Mountain") and [Lion's Head](/wiki/Lion%27s_Head_(Cape_Town) "Lion's Head (Cape Town)") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Cape_fires_%2832827624088%29.jpg/220px-Cape_fires_%2832827624088%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cape_fires_(32827624088).jpg) Satellite image of Cape Town showing the [Cape Peninsula](/wiki/Cape_Peninsula "Cape Peninsula") (left), [Cape Flats](/wiki/Cape_Flats "Cape Flats") and [False Bay](/wiki/False_Bay "False Bay") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Table_Mountain_Cape_Town_South_Africa_19Mar2018_SkySat.jpg/220px-Table_Mountain_Cape_Town_South_Africa_19Mar2018_SkySat.jpg)](/wiki/File:Table_Mountain_Cape_Town_South_Africa_19Mar2018_SkySat.jpg) Satellite image 3D of the [City Bowl](/wiki/City_Bowl "City Bowl") and Table Mountain

Cape Town is located at latitude 33.55° S (approximately the same as [Sydney](/wiki/Sydney "Sydney") and [Buenos Aires](/wiki/Buenos_Aires "Buenos Aires") and equivalent to [Casablanca](/wiki/Casablanca "Casablanca") and [Los Angeles](/wiki/Los_Angeles "Los Angeles") in the northern hemisphere) and longitude 18.25° E.

[Table Mountain](/wiki/Table_Mountain "Table Mountain"), with its near vertical cliffs and flat-topped summit over 1,000 m (3,300 ft) high, and with [Devil's Peak](/wiki/Devil%27s_Peak_(Cape_Town) "Devil's Peak (Cape Town)") and [Lion's Head](/wiki/Lion%27s_Head_(Cape_Town) "Lion's Head (Cape Town)") on either side, together form a dramatic mountainous backdrop enclosing the central area of Cape Town, the so-called [City Bowl](/wiki/City_Bowl "City Bowl"). A thin strip of cloud, known colloquially as the "tablecloth" ("Karos" in [Afrikaans](/wiki/Afrikaans "Afrikaans")), sometimes forms on top of the mountain. To the immediate south of the city, the [Cape Peninsula](/wiki/Cape_Peninsula "Cape Peninsula") is a scenic mountainous spine jutting 40 km (25 mi) southward into the [Atlantic Ocean](/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean "Atlantic Ocean") and terminating at [Cape Point](/wiki/Cape_Point "Cape Point").

There are over 70 peaks above 300 m (980 ft) within [Cape Town's official metropolitan limits](/wiki/City_of_Cape_Town "City of Cape Town"). Many of the city's suburbs lie on the large plain called the [Cape Flats](/wiki/Cape_Flats "Cape Flats"), which extends over 50 km (30 mi) to the east and joins the peninsula to the mainland. The Cape Town region is characterised by an extensive coastline, rugged mountain ranges, coastal plains and inland valleys.  

### Extent {#Extent}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=9 "Edit section: Extent")\]

The extent of Cape Town has varied considerably over time. It originated as a small settlement at the foot of Table Mountain and has grown beyond its city limits as a [metropolitan area](/wiki/Metropolitan_area "Metropolitan area") to encompass the entire [Cape Peninsula](/wiki/Cape_Peninsula "Cape Peninsula") to the south, the [Cape Flats](/wiki/Cape_Flats "Cape Flats"), the [Helderberg](/wiki/Helderberg "Helderberg") basin and part of the Steenbras catchment area to the east, and the Tygerberg hills, Blouberg and other areas to the north. [Robben Island](/wiki/Robben_Island "Robben Island") in Table Bay is also part of Cape Town. It is bounded by the Atlantic Ocean to the west, and False Bay to the south. To the north and east, the extent is demarcated by boundaries of neighbouring municipalities within the Western Cape province.

The official boundaries of the city proper extend between the [City Bowl](/wiki/City_Bowl "City Bowl") and the Atlantic Seaboard to the east and the [Southern Suburbs](/wiki/Southern_Suburbs,_Cape_Town "Southern Suburbs, Cape Town") to the south. The [City of Cape Town](/wiki/City_of_Cape_Town "City of Cape Town"), the [metropolitan municipality](/wiki/Metropolitan_municipality "Metropolitan municipality") that takes its name from the city covers the Greater Cape Town [metropolitan area](/wiki/Metropolitan_area "Metropolitan area"), known as the Cape Metropole, extending beyond the city proper itself to include a number of satellite towns, suburbs and rural areas such as [Atlantis](/wiki/Atlantis,_South_Africa "Atlantis, South Africa"), [Bellville](/wiki/Bellville,_South_Africa "Bellville, South Africa"), [Blouberg](/wiki/Blouberg,_Western_Cape "Blouberg, Western Cape"), [Brackenfell](/wiki/Brackenfell "Brackenfell"), [Durbanville](/wiki/Durbanville "Durbanville"), [Goodwood](/wiki/Goodwood,_Western_Cape "Goodwood, Western Cape"), [Gordon's Bay](/wiki/Gordon%27s_Bay "Gordon's Bay"), [Hout Bay](/wiki/Hout_Bay "Hout Bay"), [Khayelitsha](/wiki/Khayelitsha "Khayelitsha"), [Kraaifontein](/wiki/Kraaifontein "Kraaifontein"), [Kuilsrivier](/wiki/Kuils_River "Kuils River"), [Macassar](/wiki/Macassar,_Western_Cape "Macassar, Western Cape"), [Melkbosstrand](/wiki/Melkbosstrand "Melkbosstrand"), [Milnerton](/wiki/Milnerton "Milnerton"), [Muizenberg](/wiki/Muizenberg "Muizenberg"), [Noordhoek](/wiki/Noordhoek,_Cape_Town "Noordhoek, Cape Town"), [Parow](/wiki/Parow,_South_Africa "Parow, South Africa"), [Philadelphia](/wiki/Philadelphia,_South_Africa "Philadelphia, South Africa"), [Simon's Town](/wiki/Simon%27s_Town "Simon's Town"), [Somerset West](/wiki/Somerset_West "Somerset West"), and [Strand](/wiki/Strand,_Western_Cape "Strand, Western Cape") among others.^[\[63\]](#cite_note-64)^^[\[64\]](#cite_note-65)^{#cite_ref-65}

The [Cape Peninsula](/wiki/Cape_Peninsula "Cape Peninsula") is 52 km (30 mi) long from [Mouille Point](/wiki/Mouille_Point "Mouille Point") in the north to Cape Point in the south,^[\[65\]](#cite_note-Map_3318-66)^ with an area of about 470 km^2^ (180 sq mi), and it displays more topographical variety than other similar sized areas in southern Africa, and consequently spectacular scenery. There are diverse low-nutrient soils, large rocky outcrops, scree slopes, a mainly rocky coastline with embayed beaches, and considerable local variation in climatic conditions.^[\[66\]](#cite_note-Cowling_et_al_1996-67)^{#cite_ref-Cowling_et_al_1996_67-0}

The sedimentary rocks of the [Cape Supergroup](/wiki/Cape_Supergroup "Cape Supergroup"), of which parts of the Graafwater and Peninsula Formations remain, were uplifted between 280 and 21S million years ago, and were largely eroded away during the Mesozoic. The region was geologically stable during the Tertiary, which has led to slow denudation of the durable sandstones. Erosion rate and drainage has been influenced by fault lines and fractures, leaving remnant steep-sided massifs like Table Mountain surrounded by flatter slopes of deposits of the eroded material overlaying the older rocks,^[\[66\]](#cite_note-Cowling_et_al_1996-67)^{#cite_ref-Cowling_et_al_1996_67-1}

There are two internationally notable landmarks, [Table Mountain](/wiki/Table_Mountain "Table Mountain") and [Cape Point](/wiki/Cape_Point "Cape Point"), at opposite ends of the Peninsula Mountain Chain, with the [Cape Flats](/wiki/Cape_Flats "Cape Flats") and [False Bay](/wiki/False_Bay "False Bay") to the east and the [Atlantic Ocean](/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean "Atlantic Ocean") to the west. The landscape is dominated by sandstone plateaux and ridges, which generally drop steeply at their margins to the surrounding debris slopes, interrupted by a major gap at the Fish Hoek--Noordhoek valley. In the south much of the area is a low sandstone plateau with sand dunes. Maximum altitude is 1113 m on Table Mountain.^[\[66\]](#cite_note-Cowling_et_al_1996-67)^ The Cape Flats (Afrikaans: Kaapse Vlakte) is a flat, low-lying, sandy area, area to the east the Cape Peninsula, and west of the Helderberg much of which was wetland and dunes within recent history. To the north are the Tygerberg Hills and the Stellenbosch district.{#cite_ref-Cowling_et_al_1996_67-2}

The [Helderberg](/wiki/Helderberg "Helderberg") area of Greater Cape Town, previously known as the "Hottentots-Holland" area, is mostly residential, but also a wine-producing area east of the Cape Flats, west of the Hottentots Holland mountain range and south of the Helderberg mountain, from which it gets its current name. The Helderberg consists of the previous municipalities of Somerset West, Strand, Gordons Bay and a few other towns. Industry and commerce is largely in service of the area.

After the Cape Peninsula, Helderberg is the next most mountainous part of Greater Cape Town, bordered to the north and east by the highest peaks in the region along the watershed of the Helderberg and Hottentots Holland Mountains, which are part of the Cape Fold Belt with [Cape Supergroup](/wiki/Cape_Supergroup "Cape Supergroup") strata on a basement of Tygerberg Formation rocks intruded by part of the Stellenbosch granite pluton. The region includes the entire catchment of the Lourens and Sir Lowry's rivers, separated by the Schapenberg hill, and a small part of the catchment of the Eerste River to the west. The Helderberg is ecologically highly diverse, rivaling the Cape Peninsula, and has its own endemic ecoregions and several conservation areas.

To the east of the Hottentots Holland mountains is the valley of the Steenbras River, in which the [Steenbras Dam](/wiki/Steenbras_Dam "Steenbras Dam") was built as a water supply for Cape Town. The dam has been supplemented by several other dams around the western Cape, some of them considerably larger. This is almost entirely a conservation area, of high biodiversity. [Bellville](/wiki/Bellville,_South_Africa "Bellville, South Africa"), [Brackenfell](/wiki/Brackenfell "Brackenfell"), [Durbanville](/wiki/Durbanville "Durbanville"), [Kraaifontein](/wiki/Kraaifontein "Kraaifontein"), [Goodwood](/wiki/Goodwood,_Western_Cape "Goodwood, Western Cape") and [Parow](/wiki/Parow,_South_Africa "Parow, South Africa") are a few of the towns that make up the [Northern Suburbs](/wiki/Northern_Suburbs,_Cape_Town "Northern Suburbs, Cape Town") of Cape Town. In current popular culture these areas are often referred to as being beyond the "[boerewors](/wiki/Boerewors "Boerewors") curtain," a play on the term "[iron curtain](/wiki/Iron_Curtain "Iron Curtain")."

[UNESCO](/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO") declared [Robben Island](/wiki/Robben_Island "Robben Island") in the Western Cape a [World Heritage Site](/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Africa "List of World Heritage Sites in Africa") in 1999. Robben Island is located in Table Bay, some 6 km (3.7 mi) west of Bloubergstrand, a coastal suburb north of Cape Town, and stands some 30m above sea level. Robben Island has been used as a [prison](/wiki/Maximum_Security_Prison,_Robben_Island "Maximum Security Prison, Robben Island") where people were isolated, banished, and exiled for nearly 400 years. It was also used as a [leper](/wiki/Leprosy "Leprosy") colony, a post office, a grazing ground, a mental hospital, and an outpost.^[\[67\]](#cite_note-68)^{#cite_ref-68}  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Ciudad_del_Cabo_desde_Cabeza_de_Le%C3%B3n%2C_Sud%C3%A1frica%2C_2018-07-22%2C_DD_20-23_PAN.jpg/850px-Ciudad_del_Cabo_desde_Cabeza_de_Le%C3%B3n%2C_Sud%C3%A1frica%2C_2018-07-22%2C_DD_20-23_PAN.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ciudad_del_Cabo_desde_Cabeza_de_Le%C3%B3n,_Sud%C3%A1frica,_2018-07-22,_DD_20-23_PAN.jpg "Cape Town's \"City Bowl\" viewed from Lion's Head in May (late autumn)")  
[](/wiki/File:Ciudad_del_Cabo_desde_Cabeza_de_Le%C3%B3n,_Sud%C3%A1frica,_2018-07-22,_DD_20-23_PAN.jpg "File:Ciudad del Cabo desde Cabeza de León, Sudáfrica, 2018-07-22, DD 20-23 PAN.jpg")
Cape Town's "[City Bowl](/wiki/City_Bowl "City Bowl")" viewed from [Lion's Head](/wiki/Lion%27s_Head_(Cape_Town) "Lion's Head (Cape Town)") in May (late autumn)  

### Geology {#Geology}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=10 "Edit section: Geology")\]  
Main article: [Geology of Cape Town](/wiki/Geology_of_Cape_Town "Geology of Cape Town")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Geological_map_of_the_Cape_Peninsula_and_False_Bay.png/170px-Geological_map_of_the_Cape_Peninsula_and_False_Bay.png)](/wiki/File:Geological_map_of_the_Cape_Peninsula_and_False_Bay.png) Geological map of the Cape Peninsula and False Bay

The [Cape Peninsula](/wiki/Cape_Peninsula "Cape Peninsula") is a rocky and mountainous [peninsula](/wiki/Peninsula "Peninsula") that juts out into the [Atlantic Ocean](/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean "Atlantic Ocean") at the south-western extremity of the continent. At its tip is Cape Point and the [Cape of Good Hope](/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope "Cape of Good Hope"). The peninsula forms the west side of False Bay and the Cape Flats. On the east side are the Helderberg and Hottentots Holland mountains.

The three main rock formations are the late-[Precambrian](/wiki/Precambrian "Precambrian") Malmebury group (sedimentary and metamorphic rock), the Cape Granite suit, comprising the huge Peninsula, Kuilsrivier-Helderberg, and Stellenbosch batholiths, that were intruded into the Malmesbury Group about 630 million years ago, and the [Table Mountain group](/wiki/Cape_Fold_Belt#Table_Mountain_group "Cape Fold Belt") sandstones that were deposited on the eroded surface of the granite and Malmesbury series basement about 450 million years ago.

The sand, silt and mud deposits were lithified by pressure and then folded during the Cape Orogeny to form the [Cape Fold Belt](/wiki/Cape_Fold_Belt "Cape Fold Belt"), which extends in an arc along the western and southern coasts. The present landscape is due to prolonged erosion having carved out deep valleys, removing parts of the once continuous Table Mountain Group sandstone cover from over the Cape Flats and False Bay, and leaving high residual mountain ridges.^[\[68\]](#cite_note-Compton_2004-69)^{#cite_ref-Compton_2004_69-0}

At times the sea covered the Cape Flats and [Noordhoek](/wiki/Noordhoek,_Cape_Town "Noordhoek, Cape Town") valley and the Cape Peninsula was then a group of islands. During glacial periods the sea level dropped to expose the bottom of False Bay to weathering and erosion, with the last major regression leaving the entire bottom of False Bay exposed. During this period an extensive system of dunes was formed on the sandy floor of False Bay. At this time the drainage outlets lay between Rocky Bank Cape Point to the west, and between Rocky Bank and Hangklip Ridge to the east, with the watershed roughly along the line of the contact zone east of Seal Island and Whittle Rock.^[\[68\]](#cite_note-Compton_2004-69)^^[\[69\]](#cite_note-Brown_and_Magoba_2009_part_1-70)^^: Ch2^{#cite_ref-Brown_and_Magoba_2009_part_1_70-0}  

### Climate {#Climate}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: Climate")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Llandudno_Beach%2C_Cape_Town%2C_Western_Cape_Province_%286252674535%29.jpg/220px-Llandudno_Beach%2C_Cape_Town%2C_Western_Cape_Province_%286252674535%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Llandudno_Beach,_Cape_Town,_Western_Cape_Province_(6252674535).jpg) [Llandudno, Western Cape](/wiki/Llandudno,_Western_Cape "Llandudno, Western Cape") during a sunny day

Cape Town has a [Mediterranean climate](/wiki/Mediterranean_climate "Mediterranean climate") ([Köppen](/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "Köppen climate classification"): *Csb* , bordering *Csa* ),^[\[70\]](#cite_note-71)^^[\[71\]](#cite_note-72)^^[\[72\]](#cite_note-73)^ with mild, moderately wet winters and dry, warm summers. Winter, which lasts from June to September, may see large cold fronts entering for limited periods from the Atlantic Ocean with significant [precipitation](/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology) "Precipitation (meteorology)") and strong north-westerly winds. Winter months in the city average a maximum of 18 °C (64 °F) and minimum of 8.5 °C (47 °F). Winters are [snow](/wiki/Snow "Snow") and [frost](/wiki/Frost "Frost") free, except on Table Mountain and on other mountain peaks, where light accumulation of snow and frost can sometimes occur.^[\[73\]](#cite_note-WMO-74)^ Total annual rainfall in the city averages 515 mm (20.3 in) although in the [Southern Suburbs](/wiki/Southern_Suburbs,_Cape_Town "Southern Suburbs, Cape Town"), close to the mountains, rainfall is significantly higher and averages closer to 1,000 mm (39.4 in).{#cite_ref-WMO_74-0}

Summer, which lasts from December to March, is warm and dry with an average maximum of 26 °C (79 °F) and minimum of 16 °C (61 °F). The region can get uncomfortably hot when the [Berg Wind](/wiki/Berg_wind "Berg wind"), meaning "mountain wind", blows from the [Karoo](/wiki/Karoo "Karoo") interior. Spring and summer generally feature a strong wind from the south-east, known locally as the south-easter or the [Cape Doctor](/wiki/Cape_Doctor "Cape Doctor"), so called because it blows air pollution away. This wind is caused by a persistent [high-pressure system](/wiki/Pressure_system#High-pressure_system "Pressure system") over the [South Atlantic](/wiki/South_Atlantic_Ocean "South Atlantic Ocean") to the west of Cape Town, known as the [South Atlantic High](/wiki/South_Atlantic_High "South Atlantic High"), which shifts latitude seasonally, following the sun, and influencing the strength of the fronts and their northward reach. Cape Town receives about 3,100 hours of sunshine per year.^[\[74\]](#cite_note-NOAA-75)^{#cite_ref-NOAA_75-0}

Water temperatures range greatly, between 10 °C (50 °F) on the Atlantic Seaboard, to over 22 °C (72 °F) in [False Bay](/wiki/False_Bay "False Bay"). Average annual ocean surface temperatures are between 13 °C (55 °F) on the Atlantic Seaboard (similar to Californian waters, such as [San Francisco](/wiki/San_Francisco "San Francisco") or [Big Sur](/wiki/Big_Sur "Big Sur")), and 17 °C (63 °F) in False Bay (similar to Northern Mediterranean temperatures, such as [Nice](/wiki/Nice "Nice") or [Monte Carlo](/wiki/Monte_Carlo "Monte Carlo")).

Unlike other parts of the country the city does not have many [thunderstorms](/wiki/Thunderstorm "Thunderstorm"), and most of those that do occur, happen around October to December and March to April.  
{#cite_ref-enca_78-0}

#### Climate change {#Climate_change}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: Climate change")\]

A 2019 paper published in [PLOS One](/wiki/PLOS_One "PLOS One") estimated that under [Representative Concentration Pathway 4.5](/wiki/Representative_Concentration_Pathway#4.5 "Representative Concentration Pathway"), a "moderate" scenario of [climate change](/wiki/Climate_change "Climate change") where global warming reaches \~2.5--3 °C (4.5--5.4 °F) by 2100, the climate of Cape Town in the year 2050 would most closely resemble the current climate of [Perth](/wiki/Perth "Perth") in [Australia](/wiki/Australia "Australia"). The annual temperature would increase by 1.1 °C (2.0 °F), and the temperature of the coldest month by 0.3 °C (0.54 °F), while the temperature of the warmest month would be 2.3 °C (4.1 °F) higher.^[\[78\]](#cite_note-79)^^[\[79\]](#cite_note-80)^ According to [Climate Action Tracker](/wiki/Climate_Action_Tracker "Climate Action Tracker"), the current warming trajectory appears consistent with 2.7 °C (4.9 °F), which closely matches RCP 4.5.^[\[80\]](#cite_note-81)^{#cite_ref-81}

Moreover, according to the 2022 [IPCC Sixth Assessment Report](/wiki/IPCC_Sixth_Assessment_Report "IPCC Sixth Assessment Report"), Cape Town is one of 12 major African cities ([Abidjan](/wiki/Abidjan "Abidjan"), [Alexandria](/wiki/Alexandria "Alexandria"), [Algiers](/wiki/Algiers "Algiers"), Cape Town, [Casablanca](/wiki/Casablanca "Casablanca"), [Dakar](/wiki/Dakar "Dakar"), [Dar es Salaam](/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam "Dar es Salaam"), [Durban](/wiki/Durban "Durban"), [Lagos](/wiki/Lagos "Lagos"), [Lomé](/wiki/Lom%C3%A9 "Lomé"), [Luanda](/wiki/Luanda "Luanda") and [Maputo](/wiki/Maputo "Maputo")) which would be the most severely affected by future [sea level rise](/wiki/Sea_level_rise "Sea level rise"). It estimates that they would collectively sustain cumulative damages of US$65 billion under RCP 4.5 and US$86.5 billion for the high-emission scenario RCP 8.5 by the year 2050.

Additionally, RCP 8.5 combined with the hypothetical impact from [marine ice sheet instability](/wiki/Marine_ice_sheet_instability "Marine ice sheet instability") at high levels of warming would involve up to US$137.5 billion in damages,^\[*[clarification needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify "Wikipedia:Please clarify")*\]^ while the additional accounting for the "low-probability, high-damage events" may increase aggregate risks to US$187 billion for the "moderate" RCP4.5, US$206 billion for RCP8.5 and US$397 billion under the high-end ice sheet instability scenario.^[\[81\]](#cite_note-82)^ Since sea level rise would continue for about 10,000 years under every scenario of climate change, future costs of sea level rise would only increase, especially without adaptation measures.^\[*[clarification needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify "Wikipedia:Please clarify")*\]^^[\[82\]](#cite_note-83)^{#cite_ref-83}  

### Hydrology {#Hydrology}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: Hydrology")\]  
See also: [Cape Peninsula § Drainage](/wiki/Cape_Peninsula#Drainage "Cape Peninsula"), [Helderberg § Drainage](/wiki/Helderberg#Drainage "Helderberg"), and [Cape Flats § Drainage](/wiki/Cape_Flats#Drainage "Cape Flats")  

#### Sea surface temperatures {#Sea_surface_temperatures}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: Sea surface temperatures")\]  
See also: [False Bay § Waves, tides, water circulation and temperature](/wiki/False_Bay#Waves,_tides,_water_circulation_and_temperature "False Bay"); and [Cape Peninsula § Oceanography](/wiki/Cape_Peninsula#Oceanography "Cape Peninsula")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Sea_surface_temperatures_False_Bay.png/480px-Sea_surface_temperatures_False_Bay.png)](/wiki/File:Sea_surface_temperatures_False_Bay.png) Charts of sea surface temperature in and near False Bay in summer and winter^[\[83\]](#cite_note-Pfaff_et_al_2019-84)^

Cape Town's coastal water ranges from cold to mild, and the difference between the two sides of the peninsula can be dramatic. While the Atlantic Seaboard averages annual sea surface temperatures around 13 °C (55 °F), the [False Bay](/wiki/False_Bay "False Bay") coast is much warmer, averaging between 16 and 17 °C (61 and 63 °F) annually.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

In summer, False Bay water averages slightly over 20 °C (68 °F), with 22 °C (72 °F) an occasional high. Beaches located on the Atlantic Coast tend to have colder water due to the wind driven upwellings which contribute to the [Benguela Current](/wiki/Benguela_Current "Benguela Current") which originates off the Cape Peninsula, while the water at False Bay beaches may occasionally be warmer by up to 10 °C (18 °F) at the same time in summer.

In summer False Bay is thermally stratified, with a vertical temperature variation of 5 to 9˚C between the warmer surface water and cooler depths below 50 m, while in winter the water column is at nearly constant temperature at all depths. The development of a [thermocline](/wiki/Thermocline "Thermocline") is strongest around late December and peaks in late summer to early autumn.^[\[84\]](#cite_note-Coleman_2019-85)^^: 8^ In summer the south easterly winds generate a zone of upwelling near [Cape Hangklip](/wiki/Pringle_Bay "Pringle Bay"), where surface water temperatures can be 6 to 7 °C colder than the surrounding areas, and bottom temperatures below 12 °C.^[\[84\]](#cite_note-Coleman_2019-85)^^: 10^{#cite_ref-Coleman_2019_85-1}

In the summer to early autumn (January--March), cold water upwelling near Cape Hangklip causes a strong surface temperature gradient between the south-western and north-eastern corners of the bay. In winter the surface temperature tends to be much the same everywhere. In the northern sector surface temperature varies a bit more (13 to 22 °C) than in the south (14 to 20 °C) during the year.^[\[83\]](#cite_note-Pfaff_et_al_2019-84)^{#cite_ref-Pfaff_et_al_2019_84-1}

Surface temperature variation from year to year is linked to the [El Niño--Southern Oscillation](/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o%E2%80%93Southern_Oscillation "El Niño–Southern Oscillation"). During El Niño years the South Atlantic high is shifted, reducing the south-easterly winds, so upwelling and evaporative cooling are reduced and sea surface temperatures throughout the bay are warmer, while in La Niña years there is more wind and upwelling and consequently lower temperatures. Surface water heating during El Niño increases vertical stratification. The relationship is not linear.^[\[83\]](#cite_note-Pfaff_et_al_2019-84)^ Occasionally eddies from the Agulhas current will bring warmer water and vagrant sea life carried from the south and east coasts into False Bay.{#cite_ref-Pfaff_et_al_2019_84-2}  

### Flora and fauna {#Flora_and_fauna}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: Flora and fauna")\]  
Main article: [Biodiversity of Cape Town](/wiki/Biodiversity_of_Cape_Town "Biodiversity of Cape Town")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Peninsula_Sandstone_Fynbos_-_Cape_Town_8.JPG/220px-Peninsula_Sandstone_Fynbos_-_Cape_Town_8.JPG)](/wiki/File:Peninsula_Sandstone_Fynbos_-_Cape_Town_8.JPG) [Peninsula Sandstone Fynbos](/wiki/Peninsula_Sandstone_Fynbos "Peninsula Sandstone Fynbos") growing in [Table Mountain National Park](/wiki/Table_Mountain_National_Park "Table Mountain National Park").

Located in a [Conservation International](/wiki/Conservation_International "Conservation International") [biodiversity hotspot](/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot "Biodiversity hotspot") as well as the unique [Cape Floristic Region](/wiki/Cape_Floristic_Region "Cape Floristic Region"), the city of Cape Town has one of the highest levels of [biodiversity](/wiki/Biodiversity "Biodiversity") of any equivalent area in the world.^[\[85\]](#cite_note-86)^^[\[86\]](#cite_note-fri1-87)^ These protected areas are a [World Heritage Site](/wiki/World_Heritage_Site "World Heritage Site"), and an estimated 2,200 species of plants are confined to Table Mountain -- more than exist in the whole of the [United Kingdom](/wiki/United_Kingdom "United Kingdom") which has 1200 plant species and 67 endemic plant species.^[\[87\]](#cite_note-88)^^[\[88\]](#cite_note-89)^^[\[89\]](#cite_note-90)^ Many of these species, including a great many types of [proteas](/wiki/Protea "Protea"), are endemic to the mountain and can be found nowhere else.^[\[90\]](#cite_note-91)^{#cite_ref-91}

It is home to a total of 19 different [vegetation types](/wiki/Phytochorion "Phytochorion"), of which several are [endemic](/wiki/Endemic "Endemic") to the city and occur nowhere else in the world.^[\[91\]](#cite_note-92)^ It is also the only habitat of hundreds of endemic species,^[\[92\]](#cite_note-93)^ and hundreds of others which are severely restricted or threatened. This enormous species diversity is mainly because the city is uniquely located at the convergence point of several different soil types and micro-climates.^[\[93\]](#cite_note-94)^^[\[94\]](#cite_note-95)^{#cite_ref-95}

Table Mountain has an unusually rich biodiversity. Its vegetation consists predominantly of several different types of the unique and rich Cape [Fynbos](/wiki/Fynbos "Fynbos"). The main vegetation type is endangered [Peninsula Sandstone Fynbos](/wiki/Peninsula_Sandstone_Fynbos "Peninsula Sandstone Fynbos"), but [critically endangered](/wiki/Critically_endangered "Critically endangered") [Peninsula Granite Fynbos](/wiki/Peninsula_Granite_Fynbos "Peninsula Granite Fynbos"), [Peninsula Shale Renosterveld](/wiki/Peninsula_Shale_Renosterveld "Peninsula Shale Renosterveld") and [Afromontane forest](/wiki/Afromontane "Afromontane") occur in smaller portions on the mountain.

Rapid [population growth](/wiki/Population_growth "Population growth") and [urban sprawl](/wiki/Urbanisation "Urbanisation") has covered much of these ecosystems with development. Consequently, Cape Town now has over 300 [threatened](/wiki/Threatened "Threatened") plant species and 13 which are now [extinct](/wiki/Extinct "Extinct"). The [Cape Peninsula](/wiki/Cape_Peninsula "Cape Peninsula"), which lies entirely within the city of Cape Town, has the highest concentration of [threatened species](/wiki/Threatened_species "Threatened species") of any continental area of equivalent size in the world.^[\[95\]](#cite_note-96)^ Tiny remnant populations of [critically endangered](/wiki/Critically_endangered "Critically endangered") or [near extinct](/wiki/Extinct "Extinct") plants sometimes survive on road sides, pavements and sports fields.^[\[96\]](#cite_note-97)^ The remaining ecosystems are partially protected through a system of over 30 [nature reserves](/wiki/List_of_nature_reserves_in_Cape_Town "List of nature reserves in Cape Town") -- including the massive [Table Mountain National Park](/wiki/Table_Mountain_National_Park "Table Mountain National Park").^[\[97\]](#cite_note-98)^{#cite_ref-98}

Cape Town reached first place in the 2019 [iNaturalist City Nature Challenge](/w/index.php?title=INaturalist_City_Nature_Challenge&action=edit&redlink=1 "INaturalist City Nature Challenge (page does not exist)") in two out of the three categories: Most Observations, and Most Species. This was the first entry by Capetonians in this annual competition to observe and record the local biodiversity over a four-day long weekend during what is considered the worst time of the year for local observations.^[\[98\]](#cite_note-Two_Oceans-99)^ A worldwide survey suggested that the extinction rate of endemic plants from the City of Cape Town is one of the highest in the world, at roughly three per year since 1900 -- partly a consequence of the very small and localised habitats and high endemicity.^[\[99\]](#cite_note-Rebelo_2019-100)^{#cite_ref-Rebelo_2019_100-0}

Cape Town is governed by a 231-member city council elected in a system of [mixed-member proportional representation](/wiki/Mixed-member_proportional_representation "Mixed-member proportional representation"). The city is divided into 116 [wards](/wiki/Ward_(South_Africa) "Ward (South Africa)"), each of which elects a councillor by [first-past-the-post voting](/wiki/First-past-the-post_voting "First-past-the-post voting"). The remaining 115 councillors are elected from [party lists](/wiki/Party_list "Party list") so that the total number of councillors for each party is proportional to the number of votes received by that party.^[\[100\]](#cite_note-101)^^[\[101\]](#cite_note-102)^{#cite_ref-102}

In the [2021 Municipal Elections](/wiki/2021_South_African_municipal_elections "2021 South African municipal elections"), the Democratic Alliance (DA) kept its majority, this time diminished, taking 136 seats. The African National Congress lost substantially, receiving 43 of the seats.^[\[102\]](#cite_note-103)^^[\[103\]](#cite_note-104)^ The Democratic Alliance candidate for the Cape Town mayoralty, [Geordin Hill-Lewis](/wiki/Geordin_Hill-Lewis "Geordin Hill-Lewis") was elected mayor.^[\[104\]](#cite_note-105)^{#cite_ref-105}

### International relations {#International_relations}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: International relations")\]

Cape Town has nineteen active [sister city](/wiki/Sister_city "Sister city") agreements^[\[105\]](#cite_note-International_agreements_City_of_Cape_Town-106)^{#cite_ref-International_agreements_City_of_Cape_Town_106-0}

#### 2022 invasion of Ukraine {#2022_invasion_of_Ukraine}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: 2022 invasion of Ukraine")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/City_Hall_lit_in_blue_and_yellow_%283%29.jpg/220px-City_Hall_lit_in_blue_and_yellow_%283%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:City_Hall_lit_in_blue_and_yellow_(3).jpg) Cape Town City hall lit up in the colours of the Ukrainian flag as a gesture of solidarity with the country.

The City of Cape Town has expressed explicit support for Ukraine during the [2022 invasion of the country by Russia](/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine "2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine").^[\[106\]](#cite_note-107)^ To show this support the City of Cape Town lit up the Old City Hall in the colours of the [Ukrainian flag](/wiki/Flag_of_Ukraine "Flag of Ukraine") on 2 March 2022.^[\[107\]](#cite_note-Evans_2022-108)^^[\[108\]](#cite_note-109)^ This has differentiated the city from the officially [neutral foreign policy position](/wiki/South_Africa%E2%80%93Ukraine_relations#2022_Russian_invasion "South Africa–Ukraine relations") taken by the South African national government.^[\[107\]](#cite_note-Evans_2022-108)^{#cite_ref-Evans_2022_108-1}  

Demographics {#Demographics}
----------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Demographics")\]
{#cite_ref-Census2022_117-0}

|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| | Year |         |        | | 1658 |   360   |  ---   | | 1731 |  3,157  | +3.02% | | 1823 | 15,500  | +1.74% | | 1833 | 19,227  | +2.18% | | 1836 | 20,000  | +1.32% | | 1875 | 45,000  | +2.10% | | 1891 | 67,000  | +2.52% | | 1901 | 171,000 | +9.82% | | 1936 | 344,223 | +2.02% | | 1950 | 618,000 | +4.27% | | 1955 | 705,000 | +2.67% | | 1960 | 803,000 | +2.64% | | 1965 | 945,000 | +3.31% | |------|---------|--------| | | Year |           |        | | 1970 | 1,114,000 | +3.35% | | 1975 | 1,339,000 | +3.75% | | 1980 | 1,609,000 | +3.74% | | 1985 | 1,933,000 | +3.74% | | 1990 | 2,296,000 | +3.50% | | 1996 | 2,565,018 | +1.86% | | 2001 | 2,892,243 | +2.43% | | 2007 | 3,497,097 | +3.22% | | 2011 | 3,740,025 | +1.69% | | 2016 | 4,004,793 | +1.38% | | 2021 | 4,678,900 | +3.16% | | 2022 | 4,772,846 | +2.01% | |------|-----------|--------| |
| Note: Census figures (1996--2011) cover figures after 1994 reflect the greater Cape Town metropolitan municipality reflecting post-1994 reforms. **Sources:** 1658--1904,^[\[32\]](#cite_note-C1875-33)^ 1823,^[\[109\]](#cite_note-morse1823-110)^ 1833,^[\[24\]](#cite_note-Martin_1836_113-25)^ 1936,^[\[110\]](#cite_note-yearbook1936-111)^ 1950--1990,^[\[111\]](#cite_note-Mongabay-112)^ 1996,^[\[112\]](#cite_note-CT1996-113)^ 2001, and 2011 Census;^[\[113\]](#cite_note-CT2011-114)^ 2007,^[\[114\]](#cite_note-CT2007-115)^ 2016 \& 2021,^[\[115\]](#cite_note-SOCT2022-116)^ 2022^[\[116\]](#cite_note-Census2022-117)^                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   ||
[Historical population]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Cape_Town_population_pyramid.svg/220px-Cape_Town_population_pyramid.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Cape_Town_population_pyramid.svg) Cape Town population pyramid in 2011 [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Cape_Town_2011_population_density_map.svg/220px-Cape_Town_2011_population_density_map.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Cape_Town_2011_population_density_map.svg) Population density in Cape Town

According to the [South African National Census of 2011](/wiki/South_African_National_Census_of_2011 "South African National Census of 2011"), the population of the City of Cape Town metropolitan municipality -- an area that includes suburbs and [exurbs](/wiki/Exurb "Exurb") -- is 3,740,026 people. This represents an annual growth rate of 2.6% compared to the results of the [previous census in 2001](/wiki/South_African_National_Census_of_2001 "South African National Census of 2001") which found a population of 2,892,243 people.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-wc-muni-report-118)^ ^: 54^{#cite_ref-wc-muni-report_118-0}

Of those residents who were asked about their [first language](/wiki/First_language "First language"), 35.7% spoke [Afrikaans](/wiki/Afrikaans "Afrikaans"), 29.8% spoke [Xhosa](/wiki/Xhosa_language "Xhosa language") and 28.4% spoke [English](/wiki/South_African_English "South African English"). 24.8% of the population is under the age of 15, while 5.5% is 65 or older.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-wc-muni-report-118)^^: 64^ The [sex ratio](/wiki/Human_sex_ratio "Human sex ratio") is 0.96, meaning that there are slightly more women than men.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-wc-muni-report-118)^^: 55^{#cite_ref-wc-muni-report_118-2}

Of those residents aged 20 or older, 1.8% have no schooling, 8.1% have some schooling but did not finish primary school, 4.6% finished primary school but have no secondary schooling, 38.9% have some secondary schooling but did not finish [Grade 12](/wiki/Grade_12 "Grade 12"), 29.9% finished Grade 12 but have no higher education, and 16.7% have higher education.

Overall, 46.6% have at least a Grade 12 education.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-wc-muni-report-118)^^: 74^ Of those aged between 5 and 25, 67.8% are attending an educational institution.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-wc-muni-report-118)^^: 78^ Amongst those aged between 15 and 65 the unemployment rate is 23.7%.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-wc-muni-report-118)^^: 79^ The average annual household income is [R](/wiki/South_African_rand "South African rand")161,762.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-wc-muni-report-118)^^: 88^{#cite_ref-wc-muni-report_118-6}

The total number of households grew from 653,085 in 1996 to 1,068,572 in 2011, which represents an increase of 63.6%.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-wc-muni-report-118)^^: 81^ The average number of household members declined from 3,92 in 1996 to 3,50 in 2011.^[\[118\]](#cite_note-Cape_Town_2016-119)^ Of those households, 78.4% are in formal structures (houses or [flats](/wiki/Apartment "Apartment")), while 20.5% are in informal structures ([shacks](/wiki/Shanty_town "Shanty town")).^[\[117\]](#cite_note-wc-muni-report-118)^^: 81^{#cite_ref-wc-muni-report_118-8}

97.3% of City-supplied households have access to electricity,^[\[119\]](#cite_note-120)^ and 94.0% of households use [electricity](/wiki/Mains_electricity "Mains electricity") for lighting.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-wc-muni-report-118)^^: 84^ 87.3% of households have [piped water](/wiki/Water_supply "Water supply") to the dwelling, while 12.0% have piped water through a communal tap.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-wc-muni-report-118)^^: 85^ 94.9% of households have regular [refuse collection](/wiki/Refuse_collection "Refuse collection") service.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-wc-muni-report-118)^^: 86^ 91.4% of households have a [flush toilet](/wiki/Flush_toilet "Flush toilet") or [chemical toilet](/wiki/Chemical_toilet "Chemical toilet"), while 4.5% still use a bucket toilet.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-wc-muni-report-118)^^: 87^ 82.1% of households have a [refrigerator](/wiki/Refrigerator "Refrigerator"), 87.3% have a television and 70.1% have a radio. Only 34.0% have a landline telephone, but 91.3% have a cellphone. 37.9% have a computer, and 49.3% have access to the Internet (either through a computer or a cellphone).^[\[117\]](#cite_note-wc-muni-report-118)^{#cite_ref-wc-muni-report_118-13}

In 2011 over 70% of cross provincial South African migrants coming into the Western Cape settled in Cape Town; 53.64% of South African migrants into the Western Cape came from the [Eastern Cape](/wiki/Eastern_Cape "Eastern Cape"), the old Cape Colony's former native reserve, and 20.95% came from Gauteng province.^[\[120\]](#cite_note-121)^{#cite_ref-121}

According to the 2016 City of Cape Town community survey, there were 4,004,793 people in the City of Cape Town metro. Out of this population, 45.7% identified as Black African, 35.1% identified as Coloured, 16.2% identified as White and 1.6% identified as Asian.^[\[121\]](#cite_note-122)^{#cite_ref-122}

During the outbreak of the [COVID-19 pandemic in South Africa](/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_South_Africa "COVID-19 pandemic in South Africa"), local media reported that increasing numbers of wealthy and middle-class South Africans have started moving from inland areas to coastal regions of the country, most notably Cape Town, in a phenomenon referred to as "*semigration* " -- short for "semi-emigration"^[\[122\]](#cite_note-Staff_Writer-123)^^[\[123\]](#cite_note-124)^^[\[124\]](#cite_note-125)^ Declining municipal services in the rest of the country and the [South African energy crisis](/wiki/South_African_energy_crisis "South African energy crisis") are other cited reasons for semigration.^[\[125\]](#cite_note-126)^{#cite_ref-126}

The city's population is expected to grow by an additional 400,000 residents between 2020 and 2025 with 76% of those new residents falling into the low-income bracket earning less than [R](/wiki/South_African_rand "South African rand") 13,000 a month.^[\[126\]](#cite_note-127)^{#cite_ref-127}  

### Religion {#Religion}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Religion")\]  
See also: [Religion in South Africa](/wiki/Religion_in_South_Africa "Religion in South Africa")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/00000-St_Georges_Cathedral-Cape_Town-s.jpg/220px-00000-St_Georges_Cathedral-Cape_Town-s.jpg)](/wiki/File:00000-St_Georges_Cathedral-Cape_Town-s.jpg) [St George's Anglican Cathedral](/wiki/St._George%27s_Cathedral,_Cape_Town "St. George's Cathedral, Cape Town") is one of the largest and oldest religious sites in the city.

In the 2015 General Household Survey 82.3% of respondents self identified as [Christian](/wiki/Christians "Christians"), 8% as [Muslim](/wiki/Muslims "Muslims"), 3.8% as following a [traditional African religion](/wiki/Traditional_African_religions "Traditional African religions") and 3.1% as "nothing in particular."^[\[127\]](#cite_note-128)^{#cite_ref-128}

Most [places of worship](/wiki/Places_of_worship "Places of worship") in the city are Christian churches and cathedrals: [Dutch Reformed Church in South Africa (NGK)](/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church_in_South_Africa_(NGK) "Dutch Reformed Church in South Africa (NGK)"), [Zion Christian Church](/wiki/Zion_Christian_Church "Zion Christian Church"), [Apostolic Faith Mission of South Africa](/wiki/Apostolic_Faith_Mission_of_South_Africa "Apostolic Faith Mission of South Africa"), [Assemblies of God](/wiki/Assemblies_of_God "Assemblies of God"), [Baptist Union of Southern Africa](/wiki/Baptist_Union_of_Southern_Africa "Baptist Union of Southern Africa") (Baptist World Alliance), [Methodist Church of Southern Africa](/wiki/Methodist_Church_of_Southern_Africa "Methodist Church of Southern Africa") (World Methodist Council), [Anglican Church of Southern Africa](/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Southern_Africa "Anglican Church of Southern Africa") (Anglican Communion), [Presbyterian Church of Africa](/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_of_Africa "Presbyterian Church of Africa") (World Communion of Reformed Churches), [Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Cape Town](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Cape_Town "Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Cape Town") (Catholic Church),^[\[128\]](#cite_note-129)^ the [Orthodox Archbishopric of Good Hope](/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Patriarchate_of_Alexandria "Greek Orthodox Patriarchate of Alexandria") ([Greek Orthodox Cathedral of St George](/wiki/Greek_Orthodox_Cathedral_of_St_George "Greek Orthodox Cathedral of St George")^[\[129\]](#cite_note-130)^) and [the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints](/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints "The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints") (LDS Church).^[\[130\]](#cite_note-131)^{#cite_ref-131}

[Islam](/wiki/Islam "Islam") is the city's second largest religion with a [long history in Cape Town](/wiki/Islam_in_South_Africa "Islam in South Africa"),^[\[131\]](#cite_note-132)^ resulting in a number of mosques and other Muslim religious sites spread across the city,^[\[132\]](#cite_note-133)^ such as the [Auwal Mosque](/wiki/Auwal_Mosque "Auwal Mosque"), South Africa's first mosque.{#cite_ref-133}

Cape Town's significant [Jewish population](/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_South_Africa "History of the Jews in South Africa") supports a number of synagogues most notably the historic [Gardens Shul](/wiki/Gardens_Shul "Gardens Shul"), the oldest Jewish congregation in South Africa.^[\[133\]](#cite_note-forward-134)^ [Marais Road Shul](/wiki/Marais_Road_Shul "Marais Road Shul") in the city's Jewish hub, [Sea Point](/wiki/Sea_Point "Sea Point"), is the largest Jewish congregation in South Africa.^[\[134\]](#cite_note-135)^ [Temple Israel](/wiki/Temple_Israel_(Cape_Town) "Temple Israel (Cape Town)") (Cape Town Progressive Jewish Congregation) also has three temples in the city.^[\[135\]](#cite_note-136)^ There is also a [Chabad](/wiki/Chabad "Chabad") centre in Sea Point and a [Chabad on Campus](/wiki/Chabad_on_Campus_International_Foundation "Chabad on Campus International Foundation") at the [University of Cape Town](/wiki/University_of_Cape_Town "University of Cape Town"), catering to Jewish students.^[\[136\]](#cite_note-137)^{#cite_ref-137}

Other religious sites in the city include [Hindu](/wiki/Hindu "Hindu") and [Buddhist](/wiki/Buddhism "Buddhism") temples and centres.^[\[137\]](#cite_note-138)^^[\[138\]](#cite_note-139)^{#cite_ref-139}  

### Crime {#Crime}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Crime")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Smash_and_Grab_Hot_Spot%2C_Retreat_%28South_Africa%29.jpg/220px-Smash_and_Grab_Hot_Spot%2C_Retreat_%28South_Africa%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Smash_and_Grab_Hot_Spot,_Retreat_(South_Africa).jpg) [Smash and grab](/wiki/Smash_and_grab "Smash and grab") Hot Spot in [Retreat](/wiki/Retreat,_Cape_Town "Retreat, Cape Town"), Road M5

In recent years, Cape Town has experienced a resurgence in violent crime, particularly driven by gang violence in areas like the [Cape Flats](/wiki/Cape_Flats "Cape Flats"). This increase in violence is attributed to various factors, including economic inequality, unemployment, and the legacy of apartheid's spatial and social divisions.^[\[58\]](#cite_note-:3-59)^^[\[139\]](#cite_note-:4-140)^{#cite_ref-:4_140-0}

Crime in Cape Town is a serious problem which affects the [quality of life](/wiki/Quality_of_life "Quality of life") and safety of its residents and visitors. Between 2022 and 2023, Cape Town recorded the highest number of murders in a single year of any city in the world at 2,998, followed by [Johannesburg](/wiki/Johannesburg "Johannesburg") and [Durban](/wiki/Durban "Durban"), an increase of 8.6% year-on-year.^[\[140\]](#cite_note-141)^^[\[141\]](#cite_note-142)^ Household crimes including [burglary](/wiki/Burglary "Burglary") also increased in the same period.^[\[142\]](#cite_note-143)^ [Mexico](/wiki/Mexico "Mexico")'s Citizen Council for Public Security and Criminal Justice ranks it among the most violent cities in the world.^[\[143\]](#cite_note-144)^ While the [UK Foreign Office](/wiki/Foreign,_Commonwealth_and_Development_Office "Foreign, Commonwealth and Development Office") considers Cape Town safe to travel to, it notes the extremely high crime rates and highlights a particular increase on violent attacks and murders on the roads to and from [Cape Town International Airport](/wiki/Cape_Town_International_Airport "Cape Town International Airport").^[\[144\]](#cite_note-145)^^[\[145\]](#cite_note-146)^{#cite_ref-146}

At the same time, the economy has grown due to the boom in the tourism and the real estate industries.^[\[146\]](#cite_note-147)^ Since July 2019 widespread violent crime in poorer [gang dominated](/wiki/Gangs_in_South_Africa "Gangs in South Africa") areas of greater Cape Town has resulted in an ongoing military presence in these neighbourhoods.^[\[147\]](#cite_note-148)^^[\[148\]](#cite_note-149)^{#cite_ref-149}

The minibus taxi industry has been the source of a number of [violent confrontations](/wiki/Taxi_wars_in_South_Africa "Taxi wars in South Africa") in the city. The northern and eastern sections of the city was the scene of the [2021 Cape Town taxi conflict](/wiki/2021_Cape_Town_taxi_conflict "2021 Cape Town taxi conflict"), a violent turf war which led to 83 deaths. The [2023 Cape Town taxi strike](/wiki/2023_Cape_Town_taxi_strike "2023 Cape Town taxi strike") resulted in 5 recorded deaths.^[\[149\]](#cite_note-150)^^[\[150\]](#cite_note-151)^{#cite_ref-151}  

Economy {#Economy}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Economy")\]  
See also: [Economy of the Western Cape](/wiki/Economy_of_the_Western_Cape "Economy of the Western Cape")
{#cite_ref-152}

|-----------|---|---------------------------------------------------------------------------|---|---------|---|
| **Top publicly traded companies in the Cape Town/Stellenbosch region for 2021** (ranked by market capitalisation) *with Metropolitan and [JSE](/wiki/Johannesburg_Stock_Exchange "Johannesburg Stock Exchange") ranks* ||||||
| **Metro** |   | **corporation**                                                           |   | **JSE** |
| 1         |   | [Naspers](/wiki/Naspers "Naspers")                                        |   | 4       |
| 2         |   | [Capitec](/wiki/Capitec "Capitec")                                        |   | 14      |
| 3         |   | [Sanlam](/wiki/Sanlam "Sanlam")                                           |   | 20      |
| 4         |   | [Shoprite](/wiki/Shoprite_(retailer) "Shoprite (retailer)")               |   | 24      |
| 5         |   | [Pepkor](/wiki/Pepkor "Pepkor")                                           |   | 30      |
| 6         |   | [Clicks](/wiki/New_Clicks_Holdings_Limited "New Clicks Holdings Limited") |   | 32      |
| 7         |   | [Woolworths](/wiki/Woolworths_(South_Africa) "Woolworths (South Africa)") |   | 35      |
| 8         |   | [Remgro](/wiki/Remgro "Remgro")                                           |   | 37      |
| **Source:** *JSE top 40* ^[\[151\]](#cite_note-152)^                                                |||||

The city is [South Africa](/wiki/South_Africa "South Africa")'s second main economic centre and [Africa](/wiki/Africa "Africa")'s third main economic hub city. It serves as the regional manufacturing centre in the Western Cape. In 2019 the city's [GMP](/wiki/Gross_metropolitan_product "Gross metropolitan product") of R489 billion^[\[152\]](#cite_note-Cape_Town_2020-153)^ (US$33.04 billion)^[\[153\]](#cite_note-SARS_2019-154)^ represented 71.1% of the Western Cape's total [GRP](/wiki/Gross_regional_domestic_product "Gross regional domestic product") and 9.6% of South Africa's total GDP;^[\[152\]](#cite_note-Cape_Town_2020-153)^ the city also accounted for 11.1%^[\[152\]](#cite_note-Cape_Town_2020-153)^ of all employed people in the country and had a citywide [GDP per capita](/wiki/GDP_per_capita "GDP per capita") of R111,364^[\[152\]](#cite_note-Cape_Town_2020-153)^ (US$7,524).^[\[153\]](#cite_note-SARS_2019-154)^{#cite_ref-SARS_2019_154-1}

Since the [Great Recession](/wiki/Great_Recession "Great Recession"), the city's economic growth rate has mirrored South Africa's decline in growth whilst the population growth rate for the city has remained steady at around 2% a year.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-Cape_Town_2020-153)^ Around 80% of the city's economic activity is generated by the [tertiary sector](/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy "Tertiary sector of the economy") of the economy with the finance, retail, real-estate, food and beverage industries being the four largest contributors to the city's economic growth rate.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-Cape_Town_2020-153)^{#cite_ref-Cape_Town_2020_153-5}

In 2008 the city was named as the most entrepreneurial city in South Africa, with the percentage of Capetonians pursuing business opportunities almost three times higher than the national average. Those aged between 18 and 64 were 190% more likely to pursue new business, whilst in Johannesburg, the same demographic group was only 60% more likely than the national average to pursue a new business.^[\[154\]](#cite_note-155)^{#cite_ref-155}

With the highest number of successful [information technology](/wiki/Information_technology "Information technology") companies in Africa, Cape Town is an important centre for the industry on the continent.^[\[155\]](#cite_note-IT_leads-156)^ This includes an increasing number of companies in the [space industry](/wiki/Space_industry "Space industry").^[\[156\]](#cite_note-157)^ Growing at an annual rate of 8.5% and an estimated worth of R77 billion in 2010, nationwide the high tech industry in Cape Town is becoming increasingly important to the city's economy.^[\[155\]](#cite_note-IT_leads-156)^ A number of entrepreneurship initiatives and universities hosting technology startups such as [Jumo](/wiki/Jumo "Jumo"), Yoco, Aerobotics, Luno, [Rain](/wiki/Rain_(telecommunications) "Rain (telecommunications)") telecommunication and The Sun Exchange are located in the city.^[\[157\]](#cite_note-158)^{#cite_ref-158}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/2018-07-20_View_from_Wikicite_meetup_at_Wikimania_%286%29.jpg/220px-2018-07-20_View_from_Wikicite_meetup_at_Wikimania_%286%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:2018-07-20_View_from_Wikicite_meetup_at_Wikimania_(6).jpg) Skyscrapers in [City Bowl](/wiki/City_Bowl "City Bowl")
