The city has the largest film industry in the [Southern Hemisphere](/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere "Southern Hemisphere")^[\[158\]](#cite_note-159)^ generating R5 billion (US$476.19 million) in revenue and providing an estimated 6,058 direct and 2,502 indirect jobs in 2013.^[\[159\]](#cite_note-160)^ Much of the industry is based out of the [Cape Town Film Studios](/wiki/Cape_Town_Film_Studios "Cape Town Film Studios").{#cite_ref-160}  

### Major companies {#Major_companies}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Major companies")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Naspers_Media24_building.jpg/220px-Naspers_Media24_building.jpg)](/wiki/File:Naspers_Media24_building.jpg) The [Naspers Centre](/wiki/Naspers_Centre "Naspers Centre") is the headquarters of [Naspers](/wiki/Naspers "Naspers"), the largest listed company headquartered in Cape Town.

Most companies headquartered in the city are insurance companies, retail groups, publishers, design houses, fashion designers, shipping companies, petrochemical companies, architects and advertising agencies.^[\[160\]](#cite_note-161)^ Some of the most notable companies headquartered in the city are food and fashion retailer [Woolworths](/wiki/Woolworths_(South_Africa) "Woolworths (South Africa)"),^[\[161\]](#cite_note-162)^ supermarket chain [Pick n Pay Stores](/wiki/Pick_n_Pay_Stores "Pick n Pay Stores") and [Shoprite](/wiki/Shoprite_(South_Africa) "Shoprite (South Africa)"),^[\[162\]](#cite_note-163)^ [New Clicks Holdings Limited](/wiki/New_Clicks_Holdings_Limited "New Clicks Holdings Limited"), fashion retailer [Foschini Group](/wiki/Foschini_Group "Foschini Group"),^[\[163\]](#cite_note-164)^ internet service provider [MWEB](/wiki/MWEB "MWEB"), [Mediclinic International](/wiki/Mediclinic_International "Mediclinic International"), [eTV](/wiki/Etv_(South_Africa) "Etv (South Africa)"), multinational mass media giant [Naspers](/wiki/Naspers "Naspers"), and financial services giant [Sanlam](/wiki/Sanlam "Sanlam")^[\[164\]](#cite_note-165)^ and [Old Mutual Park](/wiki/Old_Mutual "Old Mutual").^[\[165\]](#cite_note-OM_history-166)^{#cite_ref-OM_history_166-0}

Other notable companies include [Belron](/wiki/Belron "Belron"), [Ceres Fruit Juices](/wiki/Ceres_Fruit_Juices "Ceres Fruit Juices"), [Coronation Fund Managers](/wiki/Coronation_Fund_Managers "Coronation Fund Managers"), [Vida e Caffè](/wiki/Vida_e_Caff%C3%A8 "Vida e Caffè"), [Capitec Bank](/wiki/Capitec_Bank "Capitec Bank"). The city is a manufacturing base for several multinational companies including, [Johnson \& Johnson](/wiki/Johnson_%26_Johnson "Johnson & Johnson"), [GlaxoSmithKline](/wiki/GlaxoSmithKline "GlaxoSmithKline"), [Levi Strauss \& Co.](/wiki/Levi_Strauss_%26_Co. "Levi Strauss & Co."), [Adidas](/wiki/Adidas "Adidas"), [Bokomo Foods](/wiki/Bokomo "Bokomo"), Yoco and [Nampak](/wiki/Nampak "Nampak").^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ [Amazon Web Services](/wiki/Amazon_Web_Services "Amazon Web Services") maintains one of its largest facilities in the world in Cape Town with the city serving as the Africa headquarters for its parent company [Amazon](/wiki/Amazon_(company) "Amazon (company)").^[\[166\]](#cite_note-167)^^[\[167\]](#cite_note-168)^{#cite_ref-168}  

### Inequality {#Inequality}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Inequality")\]

The city of Cape Town's [Gini coefficient](/wiki/Gini_coefficient "Gini coefficient") of 0.58^[\[168\]](#cite_note-169)^ is lower than South Africa's Gini coefficient of 0.7 making it more equal than the rest of the country, including any other major South African city, although still highly unequal by international standards.^[\[169\]](#cite_note-IOL_inequality-170)^^[\[170\]](#cite_note-Geni2000-171)^ Between 2001 and 2010 the city's Gini coefficient, a measure of inequality, improved by dropping from 0.59 in 2007 to 0.57 in 2010^[\[171\]](#cite_note-172)^ only to increase to 0.58 by 2017.^[\[172\]](#cite_note-Socio-economic_profile-173)^{#cite_ref-Socio-economic_profile_173-0}  

### Tourism {#Tourism}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Tourism")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Clifton_Beachs.jpg/220px-Clifton_Beachs.jpg)](/wiki/File:Clifton_Beachs.jpg) [Clifton Beach](/wiki/Clifton,_Cape_Town "Clifton, Cape Town") is one of Cape Town's most famous beaches [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Ciudad_del_Cabo%2C_Kirstenbosch_NBG_29.jpg/220px-Ciudad_del_Cabo%2C_Kirstenbosch_NBG_29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ciudad_del_Cabo,_Kirstenbosch_NBG_29.jpg) [Table Mountain](/wiki/Table_Mountain "Table Mountain") from the [Kirstenbosch National Botanical Garden](/wiki/Kirstenbosch_National_Botanical_Garden "Kirstenbosch National Botanical Garden") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Boulders_Beach_2019_2.jpg/220px-Boulders_Beach_2019_2.jpg)](/wiki/File:Boulders_Beach_2019_2.jpg) [African penguins](/wiki/African_penguin "African penguin") at [Boulders Penguin Colony](/wiki/Boulders_Beach "Boulders Beach")

The Western Cape is a highly important tourist region in South Africa; the tourism industry accounts for 9.8% of the GDP of the province and employs 9.6% of the province's workforce. In 2010, over 1.5 million international tourists visited the area.^[\[173\]](#cite_note-174)^ Cape Town is not only a popular international tourist destination in [South Africa](/wiki/South_Africa "South Africa"), but [Africa](/wiki/Africa "Africa") as a whole. This is due to its mild climate, natural setting, and well-developed infrastructure.{#cite_ref-174}

The city has several well-known natural features that attract tourists, most notably [Table Mountain](/wiki/Table_Mountain "Table Mountain"),^[\[174\]](#cite_note-175)^ which forms a large part of the [Table Mountain National Park](/wiki/Table_Mountain_National_Park "Table Mountain National Park") and is the back end of the [City Bowl](/wiki/City_Bowl,_Cape_Town "City Bowl, Cape Town"). Reaching the top of the mountain can be achieved either by hiking up, or by taking the [Table Mountain Cableway](/wiki/Table_Mountain_Cableway "Table Mountain Cableway"). [Cape Point](/wiki/Cape_Point "Cape Point") is the dramatic headland at the end of the [Cape Peninsula](/wiki/Cape_Peninsula "Cape Peninsula").^[\[175\]](#cite_note-176)^ Many tourists also drive along [Chapman's Peak Drive](/wiki/Chapman%27s_Peak "Chapman's Peak"), a narrow road that links [Noordhoek](/wiki/Noordhoek,_Cape_Town "Noordhoek, Cape Town") with [Hout Bay](/wiki/Hout_Bay,_Cape_Town "Hout Bay, Cape Town"), for the views of the Atlantic Ocean and nearby mountains. It is possible to either drive or hike up [Signal Hill](/wiki/Signal_Hill_(Cape_Town) "Signal Hill (Cape Town)") for closer views of the City Bowl and Table Mountain.^[\[176\]](#cite_note-177)^{#cite_ref-177}

Many tourists also visit [Cape Town's beaches](/wiki/Beaches_of_Cape_Town "Beaches of Cape Town"), which are popular with local residents.^[\[177\]](#cite_note-CTbeaches-178)^ It is possible to visit several different beaches in the same day, each with a different setting and atmosphere. Both coasts are popular, although the beaches in affluent [Clifton](/wiki/Clifton,_Cape_Town "Clifton, Cape Town") and elsewhere on the Atlantic Coast are better developed with restaurants and cafés, with a strip of restaurants and bars accessible to the beach at [Camps Bay](/wiki/Camps_Bay "Camps Bay").{#cite_ref-CTbeaches_178-0}

The Atlantic seaboard, known as Cape Town's [Riviera](/wiki/Riviera "Riviera"), is regarded as one of the most scenic routes in South Africa, along the slopes of the Twelve Apostles to the boulders and white sand beaches of [Llandudno](/wiki/Llandudno,_Cape_Town "Llandudno, Cape Town"), with the route ending in [Hout Bay](/wiki/Hout_Bay "Hout Bay"), a diverse suburb with a fishing and recreational boating harbour near a small island with a breeding colony of African fur seals. This suburb is also accessible by road from the Constantia valley over the mountains to the northeast, and via the picturesque [Chapman's Peak](/wiki/Chapman%27s_Peak "Chapman's Peak") drive from the residential suburb Noordhoek in the Fish Hoek valley to the south-east.^[\[178\]](#cite_note-179)^ [Boulders Beach](/wiki/Boulders_Beach "Boulders Beach") near [Simon's Town](/wiki/Simon%27s_Town "Simon's Town") is known for its colony of [African penguins](/wiki/African_penguin "African penguin").^[\[179\]](#cite_note-180)^{#cite_ref-180}

The city has several notable cultural attractions. The [Victoria \& Alfred Waterfront](/wiki/Victoria_%26_Alfred_Waterfront "Victoria & Alfred Waterfront"), built on top of part of the [docks](/wiki/Dock_(maritime) "Dock (maritime)") of the Port of Cape Town, is the city's most visited tourist attraction. It is also one of the city's most popular shopping venues, with several hundred shops as well as the [Two Oceans Aquarium](/wiki/Two_Oceans_Aquarium "Two Oceans Aquarium").^[\[180\]](#cite_note-181)^^[\[181\]](#cite_note-Sinclair_2011-182)^ The V\&A also hosts the Nelson Mandela Gateway, through which [ferries](/wiki/Ferry "Ferry") depart for [Robben Island](/wiki/Robben_Island "Robben Island").^[\[182\]](#cite_note-183)^ It is possible to take a ferry from the V\&A to [Hout Bay](/wiki/Hout_Bay,_Cape_Town "Hout Bay, Cape Town"), [Simon's Town](/wiki/Simon%27s_Town,_Cape_Town "Simon's Town, Cape Town") and the [Cape fur seal](/wiki/Cape_fur_seal "Cape fur seal") colonies on Seal and Duiker Islands. Several companies offer tours of the [Cape Flats](/wiki/Cape_Flats "Cape Flats"), a region of mostly Coloured \& Black [townships](/wiki/Township_(South_Africa) "Township (South Africa)").^[\[183\]](#cite_note-184)^{#cite_ref-184}

Within the metropolitan area, the most popular areas for visitors to stay include Camps Bay, [Sea Point](/wiki/Sea_Point "Sea Point"), the [V\&A Waterfront](/wiki/Victoria_%26_Alfred_Waterfront "Victoria & Alfred Waterfront"), the [City Bowl](/wiki/City_Bowl,_Cape_Town "City Bowl, Cape Town"), [Hout Bay](/wiki/Hout_Bay "Hout Bay"), [Constantia](/wiki/Constantia,_Cape_Town "Constantia, Cape Town"), [Rondebosch](/wiki/Rondebosch "Rondebosch"), [Newlands](/wiki/Newlands,_Cape_Town "Newlands, Cape Town"), and [Somerset West](/wiki/Somerset_West "Somerset West").^[\[184\]](#cite_note-CTtourismstats-185)^ In November 2013, Cape Town was voted the best global city in *[The Daily Telegraph](/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph "The Daily Telegraph")'s* annual Travel Awards.^[\[185\]](#cite_note-186)^ Cape Town offers tourists a range of air, land and sea-based adventure activities, including helicopter rides, [paragliding](/wiki/Paragliding "Paragliding") and [skydiving](/wiki/Skydiving "Skydiving"), snorkelling and [scuba diving](/wiki/Scuba_diving "Scuba diving"), boat trips, game-fishing, hiking, mountain biking and rock climbing. [Surfing](/wiki/Surfing "Surfing") is popular and the city hosts the [Red Bull Big Wave Africa](/wiki/Red_Bull_Big_Wave_Africa "Red Bull Big Wave Africa") surfing competition every year, and there is some local and international recreational scuba tourism.^[\[186\]](#cite_note-187)^{#cite_ref-187}

The City of Cape Town works closely with Cape Town Tourism to promote the city both locally and internationally. The primary focus of Cape Town Tourism is to represent Cape Town as a tourist destination.^[\[187\]](#cite_note-188)^^[\[188\]](#cite_note-Fin24-189)^ Cape Town Tourism receives a portion of its funding from the City of Cape Town while the remainder is made up of membership fees and own-generated funds.^[\[189\]](#cite_note-190)^ The [Tristan da Cunha](/wiki/Tristan_da_Cunha "Tristan da Cunha") government owns and operates a lodging facility in Cape Town which charges discounted rates to Tristan da Cunha residents and non-resident natives.^[\[190\]](#cite_note-191)^ Cape Town's transport system links it to the rest of South Africa; it serves as the gateway to other destinations within the province. The [Cape Winelands](/wiki/Cape_Winelands "Cape Winelands") and in particular the towns of [Stellenbosch](/wiki/Stellenbosch,_Western_Cape "Stellenbosch, Western Cape"), [Paarl](/wiki/Paarl,_Western_Cape "Paarl, Western Cape") and [Franschhoek](/wiki/Franschhoek,_Western_Cape "Franschhoek, Western Cape") are popular day trips from the city for sightseeing and [wine tasting](/wiki/Wine_tasting "Wine tasting").^[\[191\]](#cite_note-192)^^[\[192\]](#cite_note-193)^{#cite_ref-193}  

Infrastructure and services {#Infrastructure_and_services}
----------------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Infrastructure and services")\]

Most goods are handled through the Port of Cape Town or [Cape Town International Airport](/wiki/Cape_Town_International_Airport "Cape Town International Airport"). Most major shipbuilding companies have offices in Cape Town.^[\[193\]](#cite_note-194)^ The province is also a centre of energy development for the country, with the existing [Koeberg nuclear power station](/wiki/Koeberg_nuclear_power_station "Koeberg nuclear power station") providing energy for the Western Cape's needs.^[\[194\]](#cite_note-195)^{#cite_ref-195}

Greater Cape Town has four major commercial nodes, with Cape Town Central Business District containing the majority of job opportunities and office space.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ [Century City](/wiki/Century_City_(Cape_Town) "Century City (Cape Town)"), the [Bellville](/wiki/Bellville,_Western_Cape "Bellville, Western Cape")/Tygervalley strip and [Claremont](/wiki/Claremont,_Cape_Town "Claremont, Cape Town") commercial nodes are well established and contain many offices and corporate headquarters.  

### Health {#Health}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Health")\]  
See also: [List of hospitals in South Africa § Cape Metropole](/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_South_Africa#Cape_Metropole "List of hospitals in South Africa")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Groote_Schuur_Hospital%2C_Observatory%2C_Cape_Town%2C_Western_Cape._05.JPG/220px-Groote_Schuur_Hospital%2C_Observatory%2C_Cape_Town%2C_Western_Cape._05.JPG)](/wiki/File:Groote_Schuur_Hospital,_Observatory,_Cape_Town,_Western_Cape._05.JPG) [Groote Schuur Hospital](/wiki/Groote_Schuur_Hospital "Groote Schuur Hospital")

* The [Alexandra Hospital](/wiki/Alexandra_Hospital_(Cape_Town) "Alexandra Hospital (Cape Town)") is a specialist mental health care hospital in Cape Town, it provides care for complex mental health issues and intellectual disability.^[\[195\]](#cite_note-196)^{#cite_ref-196}
* [Groote Schuur Hospital](/wiki/Groote_Schuur_Hospital "Groote Schuur Hospital") is a large, government-funded, teaching hospital situated on the slopes of Devil's Peak. It was founded in 1938 and is famous for being the institution where the first human-to-human heart transplant took place. Groote Schuur is the chief academic hospital of the University of Cape Town's medical school, providing tertiary care and instruction in all the major branches of medicine. The hospital underwent major extension in 1984 when two new wings were added.
* The Hottentots Holland Hospital, also known as Helderberg Hospital, is a district hospital for the Helderberg basin located in Somerset West, and also serves surrounding areas in the Overberg district.
* Vergelegen Medi-clinic -- Private hospital in Somerset West

### Education {#Education}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Education")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/UCT_Upper_Campus_landscape_view.jpg/220px-UCT_Upper_Campus_landscape_view.jpg)](/wiki/File:UCT_Upper_Campus_landscape_view.jpg) [University of Cape Town](/wiki/University_of_Cape_Town "University of Cape Town") with the [Devil's Peak](/wiki/Devil%27s_Peak_(Cape_Town) "Devil's Peak (Cape Town)") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/CPUT_Cape_Town_Campus.jpg/220px-CPUT_Cape_Town_Campus.jpg)](/wiki/File:CPUT_Cape_Town_Campus.jpg) The Cape Town Campus of the [Cape Peninsula University of Technology](/wiki/Cape_Peninsula_University_of_Technology "Cape Peninsula University of Technology"), with [Table Mountain](/wiki/Table_Mountain "Table Mountain") in the background

Public primary and secondary schools in Cape Town are run by the [Western Cape Education Department](/wiki/Western_Cape_Education_Department "Western Cape Education Department"). This provincial department is divided into seven districts; four of these are "Metropole" districts -- Metropole Central, North, South, and East -- which cover various areas of the metropolis.^[\[196\]](#cite_note-197)^ There are also many private schools, both religious and secular. Cape Town has a well-developed higher system of [public universities](/wiki/Public_university "Public university").{#cite_ref-197}

Cape Town is served by three public universities: the [University of Cape Town](/wiki/University_of_Cape_Town "University of Cape Town") (UCT), the [University of the Western Cape](/wiki/University_of_the_Western_Cape "University of the Western Cape") (UWC) and the [Cape Peninsula University of Technology](/wiki/Cape_Peninsula_University_of_Technology "Cape Peninsula University of Technology") (CPUT). [Stellenbosch University](/wiki/Stellenbosch_University "Stellenbosch University"), while not based in the metropolitan area itself, has its main campus and administrative section 50 kilometres from the City Bowl and has additional campuses, such as the Tygerberg Faculty of Medicine and Health Sciences and the Bellville Business Park, north-west of the city in the town of [Bellville](/wiki/Bellville,_South_Africa "Bellville, South Africa").

Both the University of Cape Town and Stellenbosch University are leading universities in South Africa. This is due in large part to substantial financial contributions made to these institutions by both the public and private sector. UCT is an English-language tuition institution. It has over 21,000 students and has an MBA programme that was ranked 51st by the Financial Times in 2006.^[\[197\]](#cite_note-198)^{#cite_ref-198}

It is also the top-ranked university in Africa, being the only African university to make the world's Top 200 university list at number 146.^[\[198\]](#cite_note-199)^ Since the [African National Congress](/wiki/African_National_Congress "African National Congress") has become the country's ruling party, some restructuring of Western Cape universities has taken place and as such, traditionally non-white universities have seen increased financing, which has evidently benefitted the University of the Western Cape.^[\[199\]](#cite_note-200)^^[\[200\]](#cite_note-201)^{#cite_ref-201}

The Cape Peninsula University of Technology was formed on 1 January 2005, when two separate institutions -- [Cape Technikon](/wiki/Cape_Technikon "Cape Technikon") and [Peninsula Technikon](/wiki/Peninsula_Technikon "Peninsula Technikon") -- were merged. The new university offers education primarily in English, although one may take courses in any of South Africa's official languages. The institution generally awards the [National Diploma](/wiki/National_Diploma_(South_Africa) "National Diploma (South Africa)"). Students from the universities and high schools are involved in the South African [SEDS](/wiki/SEDS "SEDS"), Students for the Exploration and Development of Space. This is the South African SEDS, and there are many SEDS branches in other countries, preparing enthusiastic students and young professionals for the growing Space industry.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

As well as the universities, there are also several [colleges](/wiki/College "College") in and around Cape Town. Including the [College of Cape Town](/wiki/College_of_Cape_Town "College of Cape Town"), False Bay College and Northlink College. Many students use NSFAS funding to help pay for tertiary education at these TVET colleges.^[\[201\]](#cite_note-202)^ Cape Town has also become a popular [study abroad](/wiki/Study_abroad_in_the_United_States "Study abroad in the United States") destination for many international college students. Many [study abroad providers](/wiki/Study_abroad_organization "Study abroad organization") offer semester, summer, short-term, and internship programs in partnership with Cape Town universities as a chance for international students to gain intercultural understanding.{#cite_ref-202}  

### Water supply {#Water_supply}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Water supply")\]  
Main article: [Western Cape Water Supply System](/wiki/Western_Cape_Water_Supply_System "Western Cape Water Supply System")

The **Western Cape Water Supply System** (WCWSS) is a complex water supply system in the [Western Cape](/wiki/Western_Cape "Western Cape") region of [South Africa](/wiki/South_Africa "South Africa"), comprising an inter-linked system of six main dams, pipelines, tunnels and distribution networks, and a number of minor dams, some owned and operated by the [Department of Water and Sanitation](/wiki/Department_of_Water_and_Sanitation "Department of Water and Sanitation") and some by the [City of Cape Town](/wiki/City_of_Cape_Town "City of Cape Town").^[\[202\]](#cite_note-Kasrils-203)^{#cite_ref-Kasrils_203-0}  

#### Water crisis of 2017 to 2018 {#Water_crisis_of_2017_to_2018}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Water crisis of 2017 to 2018")\]  
Main article: [Cape Town water crisis](/wiki/Cape_Town_water_crisis "Cape Town water crisis")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Water_Crisis.jpg/170px-Water_Crisis.jpg)](/wiki/File:Water_Crisis.jpg) Water crisis warning in Cape Town in 2018

The Cape Town water crisis of 2017 to 2018 was a period of severe water shortage in the [Western Cape](/wiki/Western_Cape "Western Cape") region, most notably affecting the [City of Cape Town](/wiki/City_of_Cape_Town "City of Cape Town"). While dam water levels had been declining since 2015, the Cape Town water crisis peaked during mid-2017 to mid-2018 when water levels hovered between 15 and 30 percent of total dam capacity.

In late 2017, there were first mentions of plans for "Day Zero", a shorthand reference for the day when the water level of the major dams supplying the city could fall below 13.5 percent.^[\[203\]](#cite_note-USA_today-204)^^[\[204\]](#cite_note-Globe_and_Mail-205)^^[\[205\]](#cite_note-Poplak_2018-206)^ "Day Zero" would mark the start of Level 7 water restrictions, when municipal water supplies would be largely switched off and it was envisioned that residents could have to queue for their daily ration of water. If this had occurred, it would have made the City of Cape Town the first major city in the world to run out of water.^[\[206\]](#cite_note-Booysen_et_al_2019-207)^^[\[207\]](#cite_note-Booysen_et_al_2019a-208)^{#cite_ref-Booysen_et_al_2019a_208-0}

The city of Cape Town implemented significant water restrictions in a bid to curb water usage, and succeeded in reducing its daily water usage by more than half to around 500 million litres (130,000,000 US gal) per day in March 2018.^[\[208\]](#cite_note-Narrandes_2018-209)^ The fall in water usage led the city to postpone its estimate for "Day Zero", and strong rains starting in June 2018 led to dam levels recovering.^[\[209\]](#cite_note-Myburgh_2018-210)^{#cite_ref-Myburgh_2018_210-0}

In September 2018, with dam levels close to 70 percent, the city began easing water restrictions, indicating that the worst of the water crisis was over.^[\[210\]](#cite_note-reduce-sep2018-211)^ Good rains in 2020 effectively broke the drought and resulting water shortage when dam levels reached 95 percent.^[\[211\]](#cite_note-After_drought-212)^ Concerns have been raised, however, that unsustainble demand and limited water supply could result in future drought events.^[\[212\]](#cite_note-213)^{#cite_ref-213}  

### Transport {#Transport}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Transport")\]  

#### Air {#Air}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Air")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/2013.01.03_Ciudad_del_Cabo%2C_ZA_%2828%29.JPG/220px-2013.01.03_Ciudad_del_Cabo%2C_ZA_%2828%29.JPG)](/wiki/File:2013.01.03_Ciudad_del_Cabo,_ZA_(28).JPG) [Cape Town International Airport](/wiki/Cape_Town_International_Airport "Cape Town International Airport")

[Cape Town International Airport](/wiki/Cape_Town_International_Airport "Cape Town International Airport") serves both domestic and international flights.^[\[213\]](#cite_note-214)^ It is the second-largest airport in South Africa and serves as a major gateway for travellers to the Cape region. Cape Town has regularly scheduled services to [Southern Africa](/wiki/Southern_Africa "Southern Africa"), [East Africa](/wiki/East_Africa "East Africa"), [Mauritius](/wiki/Mauritius "Mauritius"), [Middle East](/wiki/Middle_East "Middle East"), [Far East](/wiki/Far_East "Far East"), [Europe](/wiki/Europe "Europe"), [Brazil](/wiki/Brazil "Brazil") and the [United States](/wiki/United_States "United States") as well as eleven domestic destinations.^[\[214\]](#cite_note-215)^ Cape Town International Airport opened a brand new central terminal building that was developed to handle an expected increase in air traffic as tourism numbers increased in the lead-up to the tournament of the [2010 FIFA World Cup](/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup "2010 FIFA World Cup").^[\[215\]](#cite_note-216)^{#cite_ref-216}

Other renovations include several large new parking garages, a revamped domestic departure terminal, a new Bus Rapid Transit system station and a new double-decker road system. The airport's cargo facilities are also being expanded and several large empty plots are being developed into [office space](/wiki/Office "Office") and hotels.

Cape Town is one of five internationally recognised [Antarctic gateway cities](/wiki/Antarctic_Gateway_Cities "Antarctic Gateway Cities") with transportation connections. Since 2021, commercial flights have operated from Cape Town to [Wolf's Fang Runway](/wiki/Wolfs_Fang_Runway "Wolfs Fang Runway"), Antarctica.^[\[216\]](#cite_note-217)^ The Cape Town International Airport was among the winners of the World Travel Awards for being Africa's leading airport.^[\[217\]](#cite_note-218)^ Cape Town International Airport is located 18 km from the [Central Business District](/wiki/Central_Business_District "Central Business District").^[\[218\]](#cite_note-219)^{#cite_ref-219}  

#### Sea {#Sea}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Sea")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/2011-02-06_14-34-03_South_Africa_-_Foreshore.jpg/220px-2011-02-06_14-34-03_South_Africa_-_Foreshore.jpg)](/wiki/File:2011-02-06_14-34-03_South_Africa_-_Foreshore.jpg) The [Port of Cape Town](/wiki/Port_of_Cape_Town "Port of Cape Town") is a major transport node in southern Africa. In addition to moving freight it also serves as a major repair site for ships and oil rigs.

Cape Town has a long tradition as a port city, and its role as a re-provisioning stop at the midpoint of the [Cape Route](/wiki/Cape_Route "Cape Route") gained it the nicknames "Tavern of the Seas" and "Tavern of the Indian Ocean".^[\[219\]](#cite_note-220)^ The [Port of Cape Town](/wiki/Port_of_Cape_Town "Port of Cape Town"), the city's main port, is in Table Bay directly to the north of the CBD.{#cite_ref-220}

The port is a hub for ships in the southern Atlantic: it is located along one of the busiest shipping corridors in the world, and acts as a stopover point for goods en route to or from Latin America and Asia. It is also an entry point into the South African market.^[\[220\]](#cite_note-EU_Handbook_2020-221)^ It is the second-busiest container port in South Africa after [Durban](/wiki/Durban "Durban"). In 2004, it handled 3,161 ships and 9.2 million tonnes of cargo.^[\[221\]](#cite_note-222)^{#cite_ref-222}

[Simon's Town](/wiki/Simon%27s_Town "Simon's Town") Harbour on the False Bay coast of the Cape Peninsula is the main operational base of the [South African Navy](/wiki/South_African_Navy "South African Navy").

Until the 1970s the city was served by the [Union Castle Line](/wiki/Union_Castle_Line "Union Castle Line") with service to the United Kingdom and St Helena.^[\[222\]](#cite_note-223)^ The [RMS *St Helena*](/wiki/RMS_St_Helena_(1989) "RMS St Helena (1989)") provided passenger and cargo service between Cape Town and [St Helena](/wiki/St_Helena "St Helena") until the opening of [St Helena Airport](/wiki/St_Helena_Airport "St Helena Airport").^[\[223\]](#cite_note-224)^{#cite_ref-224}

The cargo vessel M/V *Helena* , under AW Shipping Management, takes a limited number of passengers,^[\[224\]](#cite_note-Cargoships-225)^ between Cape Town and St Helena and [Ascension Island](/wiki/Ascension_Island "Ascension Island") on its voyages.^[\[225\]](#cite_note-226)^ Multiple vessels also take passengers to and from [Tristan da Cunha](/wiki/Tristan_da_Cunha "Tristan da Cunha"), inaccessible by aircraft, to and from Cape Town.^[\[226\]](#cite_note-227)^ In addition [NSB Niederelbe Schiffahrtsgesellschaft](/w/index.php?title=NSB_Niederelbe_Schiffahrtsgesellschaft&action=edit&redlink=1 "NSB Niederelbe Schiffahrtsgesellschaft (page does not exist)") \[[de](https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/NSB_Niederelbe_Schiffahrtsgesellschaft "de:NSB Niederelbe Schiffahrtsgesellschaft")\] takes passengers on its cargo service to the [Canary Islands](/wiki/Canary_Islands "Canary Islands") and [Hamburg](/wiki/Hamburg "Hamburg"), [Germany](/wiki/Germany "Germany").^[\[224\]](#cite_note-Cargoships-225)^{#cite_ref-Cargoships_225-1}  

#### Rail {#Rail}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Rail")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/X%27trapolis_Mega_on_Kalk_Bay_bridge_Dec_2023.jpg/220px-X%27trapolis_Mega_on_Kalk_Bay_bridge_Dec_2023.jpg)](/wiki/File:X%27trapolis_Mega_on_Kalk_Bay_bridge_Dec_2023.jpg) [Metrorail](/wiki/Metrorail_(Western_Cape) "Metrorail (Western Cape)") train near [Kalk Bay](/wiki/Kalk_Bay "Kalk Bay") station.

The [Shosholoza Meyl](/wiki/Shosholoza_Meyl "Shosholoza Meyl") is the passenger rail operations of [Spoornet](/wiki/Spoornet "Spoornet") and operates one long-distance passenger rail service from Cape Town as of 2024: a weekly service to and from [Johannesburg](/wiki/Johannesburg "Johannesburg") via [Kimberley](/wiki/Kimberley,_South_Africa "Kimberley, South Africa"). These trains terminate at [Cape Town railway station](/wiki/Cape_Town_railway_station "Cape Town railway station") and make a stop at [Bellville](/wiki/Bellville_railway_station "Bellville railway station"). Cape Town also terminates 2 luxury tourist train routes as of 2024 operated by the [Ceres Rail Company](/w/index.php?title=Ceres_Rail_Company&action=edit&redlink=1 "Ceres Rail Company (page does not exist)"), traveling from the [Waterfront](/wiki/V%26A_Waterfront "V&A Waterfront") to [Simon's Town](/wiki/Simon%27s_Town "Simon's Town") and [Grabouw](/wiki/Grabouw "Grabouw") respectively.

[Metrorail](/wiki/Metrorail_(Western_Cape) "Metrorail (Western Cape)") operates a [commuter rail](/wiki/Commuter_rail "Commuter rail") service in Cape Town and the surrounding area. The Metrorail network consists of 96 stations throughout the suburbs and outskirts of Cape Town.  

#### Road {#Road}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Road")\]

Cape Town is the origin of three [national roads](/wiki/National_Roads_in_South_Africa "National Roads in South Africa"). The [N1](/wiki/N1_(South_Africa) "N1 (South Africa)") and [N2](/wiki/N2_(South_Africa) "N2 (South Africa)") begin in the foreshore area near the City Centre and the [N7](/wiki/N7_(South_Africa) "N7 (South Africa)"), which runs North toward [Namibia](/wiki/Namibia "Namibia"). The N1 runs East-North-East from Cape Town through the towns of [Goodwood](/wiki/Goodwood,_Western_Cape "Goodwood, Western Cape"), [Parow](/wiki/Parow,_South_Africa "Parow, South Africa"), [Bellville](/wiki/Bellville,_Cape_Town "Bellville, Cape Town"), [Brackenfell](/wiki/Brackenfell,_Cape_Town "Brackenfell, Cape Town") and [Kraaifontein](/wiki/Kraaifontein "Kraaifontein") before continuing towards [Paarl](/wiki/Paarl "Paarl"). It connects Cape Town to major cities further inland, namely [Bloemfontein](/wiki/Bloemfontein "Bloemfontein"), [Johannesburg](/wiki/Johannesburg "Johannesburg"), and [Pretoria](/wiki/Pretoria "Pretoria") An older at-grade road, the [R101](/wiki/R101_road_(South_Africa) "R101 road (South Africa)"), runs parallel to the N1 from Bellville.

The N2 runs East-South-East through [Rondebosch](/wiki/Rondebosch "Rondebosch"), [Guguletu](/wiki/Guguletu "Guguletu"), [Khayelitsha](/wiki/Khayelitsha "Khayelitsha"), [Macassar](/wiki/Macassar,_Western_Cape "Macassar, Western Cape") to [Somerset West](/wiki/Somerset_West "Somerset West"). It becomes a multiple-carriageway, at-grade road from the intersection with the [R44](/wiki/R44_road_(South_Africa) "R44 road (South Africa)") onward. The N2 continues east along the coast, linking Cape Town with Somerset West and the coastal cities of [Mossel Bay](/wiki/Mossel_Bay "Mossel Bay"), [George](/wiki/George,_Western_Cape "George, Western Cape"), [Port Elizabeth](/wiki/Port_Elizabeth "Port Elizabeth"), [East London](/wiki/East_London,_South_Africa "East London, South Africa") and [Durban](/wiki/Durban "Durban"). An older at-grade road, the [R102](/wiki/R102_(South_Africa) "R102 (South Africa)"), runs parallel to the N1 initially, before veering south at Bellville, to join the N2 at Somerset West via the towns of [Kuilsrivier](/wiki/Kuils_River "Kuils River") and [Eersterivier](/wiki/Eerste_River,_Western_Cape "Eerste River, Western Cape"). The N7 originates from the N1 at Wingfield Interchange near Edgemead. It begins, initially as a highway, but becoming an at-grade road from the intersection with the M5 onward.
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Cape_Town_N2.jpg/220px-Cape_Town_N2.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cape_Town_N2.jpg) The [N2](/wiki/N2_(South_Africa) "N2 (South Africa)") as it enters the city centre.

There are also a number of [regional routes](/wiki/Provincial_route_(South_Africa) "Provincial route (South Africa)") linking Cape Town with surrounding areas. The [R27](/wiki/R27_road_(South_Africa) "R27 road (South Africa)") originates from the N1 near the Foreshore and runs north parallel to the N7, but nearer to the coast. It passes through the suburbs of [Milnerton](/wiki/Milnerton,_Cape_Town "Milnerton, Cape Town"), [Table View](/wiki/Table_View,_Cape_Town "Table View, Cape Town") and [Bloubergstrand](/wiki/Bloubergstrand,_Cape_Town "Bloubergstrand, Cape Town") and links the city to the West Coast, ending at the town of [Velddrif](/wiki/Velddrif "Velddrif"). The [R44](/wiki/R44_road_(South_Africa) "R44 road (South Africa)") enters the east of the metro from the north, from [Stellenbosch](/wiki/Stellenbosch "Stellenbosch"). It connects Stellenbosch to Somerset West, then crosses the N2 to [Strand](/wiki/Strand,_Western_Cape "Strand, Western Cape") and [Gordon's Bay](/wiki/Gordon%27s_Bay "Gordon's Bay"). It exits the metro heading south hugging the coast, leading to the towns of [Betty's Bay](/wiki/Betty%27s_Bay "Betty's Bay") and [Kleinmond](/wiki/Kleinmond "Kleinmond").

Of the three-digit routes, the [R300](/wiki/R300_road_(South_Africa) "R300 road (South Africa)") is an expressway linking the N1 at [Brackenfell](/wiki/Brackenfell "Brackenfell") to the N2 near [Mitchells Plain](/wiki/Mitchells_Plain "Mitchells Plain") and the [Cape Town International Airport](/wiki/Cape_Town_International_Airport "Cape Town International Airport"). The [R302](/wiki/R302_road_(South_Africa) "R302 road (South Africa)") runs from the R102 in Bellville, heading north across the N1 through [Durbanville](/wiki/Durbanville "Durbanville") leaving the metro to [Malmesbury](/wiki/Malmesbury,_Western_Cape "Malmesbury, Western Cape"). The [R304](/wiki/R304_road_(South_Africa) "R304 road (South Africa)") enters the northern limits of the metro from Stellenbosch, running NNW before veering west to cross the N7 at [Philadelphia](/wiki/Philadelphia,_Western_Cape "Philadelphia, Western Cape") to end at [Atlantis](/wiki/Atlantis,_Western_Cape "Atlantis, Western Cape") at a junction with the [R307](/wiki/R307_road_(South_Africa) "R307 road (South Africa)"). This R307 starts north of [Koeberg](/wiki/Koeberg "Koeberg") from the R27 and, after meeting the R304, continues north to [Darling](/wiki/Darling,_Western_Cape "Darling, Western Cape"). The [R310](/wiki/R310_road_(South_Africa) "R310 road (South Africa)") originates from [Muizenberg](/wiki/Muizenberg "Muizenberg") and runs along the coast, to the south of Mitchell's Plain and Khayelitsha, before veering north-east, crossing the N2 west of Macassar, and exiting the metro heading to Stellenbosch.

Cape Town, like most South African cities, uses [Metropolitan](/wiki/Metropolitan_Routes_in_Cape_Town "Metropolitan Routes in Cape Town") or "M" routes for important intra-city routes, a layer below National (N) roads and Regional (R) routes. Each city's M roads are independently numbered. Most are at-grade roads. The [M3](/wiki/M3_(Cape_Town) "M3 (Cape Town)") splits from the N2 and runs to the south along the eastern slopes of Table Mountain, connecting the City Bowl with [Muizenberg](/wiki/Muizenberg "Muizenberg"). Except for a section between Rondebosch and Newlands that has at-grade intersections, this route is a highway. The [M5](/wiki/M5_(Cape_Town) "M5 (Cape Town)") splits from the N1 further east than the M3, and links the Cape Flats to the CBD. It is a highway as far as the interchange with the M68 at Ottery, before continuing as an at-grade road. Cape Town has the worst traffic congestion in [South Africa](/wiki/South_Africa "South Africa").^[\[227\]](#cite_note-228)^^[\[228\]](#cite_note-229)^{#cite_ref-229}  

#### Buses {#Buses}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Buses")\]

[Golden Arrow Bus Services](/wiki/Golden_Arrow_Bus_Services "Golden Arrow Bus Services") operates scheduled bus services in the Cape Town metropolitan area. Several companies run long-distance bus services from Cape Town to the other cities in South Africa.  

##### MyCiTi {#MyCiTi}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: MyCiTi")\]  
Main article: [MyCiTi](/wiki/MyCiTi "MyCiTi")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/MyCiti_BRT_Adderley_station_%2821812360016%29.jpg/220px-MyCiti_BRT_Adderley_station_%2821812360016%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:MyCiti_BRT_Adderley_station_(21812360016).jpg) [MyCiTi](/wiki/MyCiTi "MyCiTi") station and bus

Cape Town has a public transport system in about 10% of the city, running north to south along the west coastline of the city, comprising Phase 1 of the IRT system. This is known as the MyCiTi service.^[\[229\]](#cite_note-230)^{#cite_ref-230}

MyCiTi Phase 1 includes services linking the Airport to the Cape Town inner city, as well as the following areas: [Blouberg](/wiki/Bloubergstrand "Bloubergstrand") / [Table View](/wiki/Table_View "Table View"), [Dunoon](/wiki/Dunoon,_Cape_Town "Dunoon, Cape Town"), [Atlantis](/wiki/Atlantis,_Western_Cape "Atlantis, Western Cape") and [Melkbosstrand](/wiki/Melkbosstrand "Melkbosstrand"), [Milnerton](/wiki/Milnerton,_Cape_Town "Milnerton, Cape Town"), Paarden Eiland, [Century City](/wiki/Century_City,_Cape_Town "Century City, Cape Town"), [Salt River](/wiki/Salt_River,_Cape_Town "Salt River, Cape Town") and [Walmer Estate](/wiki/Walmer_Estate,_Cape_Town "Walmer Estate, Cape Town"), and all suburbs of the [City Bowl](/wiki/City_Bowl "City Bowl") and [Atlantic Seaboard](#Atlantic_Seaboard) all the way to [Llandudno](/wiki/Llandudno,_Cape_Town "Llandudno, Cape Town") and [Hout Bay](/wiki/Hout_Bay,_Cape_Town "Hout Bay, Cape Town").^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

The MyCiTi N2 Express service consists of four routes each linking the Cape Town inner city and [Khayelitsha](/wiki/Khayelitsha "Khayelitsha") and [Mitchells Plain](/wiki/Mitchells_Plain "Mitchells Plain") on the [Cape Flats](/wiki/Cape_Flats "Cape Flats").^[\[230\]](#cite_note-231)^{#cite_ref-231}

The service use high floor articulated and standard size buses in dedicated busways, low floor articulated and standard size buses on the N2 Express service, and smaller 9 m (30 ft) [Optare](/wiki/Optare "Optare") buses in suburban and inner city areas. It offers [universal access](/wiki/Accessibility#Transportation "Accessibility") through level boarding and numerous other measures, and requires cashless fare payment using the [EMV](/wiki/EMV "EMV") compliant smart card system, called myconnect. Headway of services (i.e. the time between buses on the same route) range from three to twenty minutes in peak times to an hour in off-peak times.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^  

#### Taxis {#Taxis}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Taxis")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Cape_Town_Taxicab_in_Campsbay.jpg/220px-Cape_Town_Taxicab_in_Campsbay.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cape_Town_Taxicab_in_Campsbay.jpg) A fleet of privately-owned taxis in [Camps Bay](/wiki/Camps_Bay "Camps Bay")

Cape Town has various kinds of taxis available, including those obtained through ride-hailing services such as [Bolt](/wiki/Bolt_(company) "Bolt (company)") and [Uber](/wiki/Uber "Uber").

Taxis are either [metered taxis](/wiki/Taxicab "Taxicab") or [minibus taxis](/wiki/Minibus_taxi "Minibus taxi"). Metered taxis can be found at transport hubs as well as other tourist establishments, while minibus taxis can be found at taxi ranks, and, commonly, travelling along main streets.^[\[231\]](#cite_note-232)^ Minibus taxis can be hailed from the road.^[\[232\]](#cite_note-233)^{#cite_ref-233}

Cape Town metered taxi cabs mostly operate in the city bowl, suburbs and Cape Town International Airport areas. Large companies that operate fleets of cabs can be reached by phone and are cheaper than the single operators that apply for hire from taxi ranks and [Victoria and Alfred Waterfront](/wiki/Victoria_and_Alfred_Waterfront "Victoria and Alfred Waterfront"). There are about one thousand meter taxis in Cape Town. Their rates vary from R8 per kilometre to about R15 per kilometre. The larger taxi companies in Cape Town are Excite Taxis, Cabnet and Intercab and single operators are reachable by cellular phone. The seven seated Toyota Avanza are the most popular with larger Taxi companies. Meter cabs are mostly used by tourists and are safer to use than minibus taxis.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

Minibus taxis are the standard form of transport for the majority of the population who cannot afford private vehicles.^[\[233\]](#cite_note-234)^ Although essential, these taxis are often poorly maintained and are frequently not road-worthy. These taxis make frequent unscheduled stops to pick up passengers, which can cause accidents.^[\[234\]](#cite_note-235)^^[\[235\]](#cite_note-236)^ With the high demand for transport by the working class of South Africa, minibus taxis are often filled over their legal passenger allowance. Minibuses are generally owned and operated in fleets.^[\[236\]](#cite_note-237)^{#cite_ref-237}  

Culture {#Culture}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Culture")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Kaapse_Klopse_marching_through_Cape_Town_%282017%29.jpg/220px-Kaapse_Klopse_marching_through_Cape_Town_%282017%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Kaapse_Klopse_marching_through_Cape_Town_(2017).jpg) [Cape Town Minstrel Carnival](/wiki/Kaapse_Klopse "Kaapse Klopse") (2017)

Cape Town is noted for its architectural heritage, with the highest density of [Cape Dutch](/wiki/Cape_Dutch_architecture "Cape Dutch architecture") style buildings in the world. Cape Dutch style, which combines the architectural traditions of the Netherlands, Germany, France and Indonesia, is most visible in [Constantia](/wiki/Constantia,_Cape_Town "Constantia, Cape Town"), the [old government buildings](/wiki/Houses_of_Parliament,_Cape_Town "Houses of Parliament, Cape Town") in the Central Business District, and along [Long Street](/wiki/Long_Street_(Cape_Town) "Long Street (Cape Town)").^[\[237\]](#cite_note-238)^^[\[238\]](#cite_note-239)^{#cite_ref-239}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Groot_Constantia_-_2.jpg/220px-Groot_Constantia_-_2.jpg)](/wiki/File:Groot_Constantia_-_2.jpg) [Groot Constantia](/wiki/Groot_Constantia "Groot Constantia") is a good example of Cape Dutch architecture.

The annual [Cape Town Minstrel Carnival](/wiki/Coon_Carnival "Coon Carnival"), also known by its Afrikaans name of *Kaapse Klopse* , is a large [minstrel](/wiki/Minstrel "Minstrel") festival held annually on 2 January or *"Tweede Nuwe Jaar"* (Second New Year). Competing teams of minstrels parade in brightly coloured costumes, performing [Cape Jazz](/wiki/Cape_Jazz "Cape Jazz"), either carrying colourful umbrellas or playing an array of musical instruments. The [Artscape Theatre Centre](/wiki/Artscape_Theatre_Centre "Artscape Theatre Centre") is the largest performing arts venue in Cape Town.^[\[239\]](#cite_note-240)^ The city was named the [World Design Capital](/wiki/World_Design_Capital "World Design Capital") for 2014 by the [International Council of Societies of Industrial Design](/wiki/International_Council_of_Societies_of_Industrial_Design "International Council of Societies of Industrial Design").^[\[240\]](#cite_note-241)^{#cite_ref-241}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Holi_One_We_Are_One_Colour_Festival_South_Africa_2013.jpg/220px-Holi_One_We_Are_One_Colour_Festival_South_Africa_2013.jpg)](/wiki/File:Holi_One_We_Are_One_Colour_Festival_South_Africa_2013.jpg) [Holi](/wiki/Holi "Holi") festival at the [Grand Parade](/wiki/Grand_Parade_(Cape_Town) "Grand Parade (Cape Town)")

The city also encloses the 36 hectare [Kirstenbosch National Botanical Garden](/wiki/Kirstenbosch_National_Botanical_Garden "Kirstenbosch National Botanical Garden") that contains protected natural forest and [fynbos](/wiki/Fynbos "Fynbos") along with a variety of animals and birds. There are over 7,000 species in cultivation at Kirstenbosch, including many rare and threatened species of the [Cape Floristic Region](/wiki/Cape_Floristic_Region "Cape Floristic Region"). In 2004 this Region, including Kirstenbosch, was declared a UNESCO [World Heritage Site](/wiki/World_Heritage_Site "World Heritage Site").^[\[241\]](#cite_note-242)^{#cite_ref-242}

[Whale watching](/wiki/Whale_watching "Whale watching") is popular amongst tourists: [southern right whales](/wiki/Southern_right_whale "Southern right whale") and [humpback whales](/wiki/Humpback_whale "Humpback whale") are seen off the coast during the breeding season (August to November) and [Bryde's whales](/wiki/Bryde%27s_whale "Bryde's whale") and [orca](/wiki/Orca "Orca") can be seen any time of the year.^[\[242\]](#cite_note-CTwhale-243)^ The nearby town of [Hermanus](/wiki/Hermanus "Hermanus") is known for its Whale Festival, but whales can also be seen in False Bay.^[\[242\]](#cite_note-CTwhale-243)^ [Heaviside's dolphins](/wiki/Heaviside%27s_dolphin "Heaviside's dolphin") are endemic to the area and can be seen from the coast north of Cape Town; [dusky dolphins](/wiki/Dusky_dolphin "Dusky dolphin") live along the same coast and can occasionally be seen from the ferry to Robben Island.^[\[242\]](#cite_note-CTwhale-243)^{#cite_ref-CTwhale_243-2}

The only complete windmill in South Africa is [Mostert's Mill](/wiki/Mostert%27s_Mill "Mostert's Mill"), [Mowbray](/wiki/Mowbray,_Cape_Town "Mowbray, Cape Town"). It was built in 1796 and restored in 1935 and again in 1995.
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Mosterts_Mill.jpg/220px-Mosterts_Mill.jpg)](/wiki/File:Mosterts_Mill.jpg) [Mostert's Mill](/wiki/Mostert%27s_Mill "Mostert's Mill") in Cape Town.  

### Cuisine {#Cuisine}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Cuisine")\]  
See also: [South African cuisine](/wiki/South_African_cuisine "South African cuisine")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Cape_Town_-_Vegan_Lekker_Nuggy_Gatsby_in_restaurant_Lekker_Vegan.jpg/220px-Cape_Town_-_Vegan_Lekker_Nuggy_Gatsby_in_restaurant_Lekker_Vegan.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cape_Town_-_Vegan_Lekker_Nuggy_Gatsby_in_restaurant_Lekker_Vegan.jpg) A gatsby sandwich, freshly prepared

Food originating from or synonymous with Cape Town includes the savoury sweet spiced meat dish [Bobotie](/wiki/Bobotie "Bobotie") that dates from the 17th century. The [Gatsby](/wiki/Gatsby_(sandwich) "Gatsby (sandwich)"), a sandwich filled with [slap chips](/wiki/Slap_chips "Slap chips") and other toppings, was first served in 1976 in the suburb of [Athlone](/wiki/Athlone,_Cape_Town "Athlone, Cape Town") and is also synonymous with the city.^[\[243\]](#cite_note-244)^ The [koe'sister](/wiki/Koe%27sister "Koe'sister") is a traditional [Cape Malay](/wiki/Cape_Malays "Cape Malays") pastry described as a cinnamon infused dumpling with a cake-like texture, finished off with a sprinkling of desiccated coconut.^[\[244\]](#cite_note-245)^{#cite_ref-245}

[Malva pudding](/wiki/Malva_pudding "Malva pudding") (sometimes known as Cape Malva pudding) is a sticky sweet dessert often served with hot custard is also associated with the city and dates back to the 17th century.^[\[245\]](#cite_note-246)^ A related dessert dish, [Cape Brandy Pudding](/wiki/Cape_Brandy_Pudding "Cape Brandy Pudding"), is also associated with the city and surrounding region.^[\[246\]](#cite_note-247)^ Cape Town is also the home of the [South African wine](/wiki/South_African_wine "South African wine") industry with the first wine produced in the country being bottled in the city; a number of notable wineries still exist in the city including [Groot Constantia](/wiki/Groot_Constantia "Groot Constantia") and [Klein Constantia](/wiki/Klein_Constantia "Klein Constantia").{#cite_ref-247}  

### Media {#Media}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Media")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Cape_Town_TV_news_van.jpg/220px-Cape_Town_TV_news_van.jpg)](/wiki/File:Cape_Town_TV_news_van.jpg) A news van owned by [Cape Town TV](/wiki/Cape_Town_TV "Cape Town TV") outside the [Houses of Parliament](/wiki/Houses_of_Parliament,_Cape_Town "Houses of Parliament, Cape Town")

Several newspapers, magazines and printing facilities have their offices in the city. [Independent News and Media](/wiki/Independent_News_and_Media "Independent News and Media") publishes the major English language papers in the city, the *[Cape Argus](/wiki/Cape_Argus "Cape Argus")* and the *[Cape Times](/wiki/Cape_Times "Cape Times")* . [Naspers](/wiki/Naspers "Naspers"), the largest media conglomerate in South Africa, publishes *[Die Burger](/wiki/Die_Burger "Die Burger")* , the major Afrikaans language paper.^[\[247\]](#cite_note-248)^{#cite_ref-248}

Cape Town has many local community [newspapers](/wiki/Newspapers "Newspapers"). Some of the largest community newspapers in English are the *Athlone News* from [Athlone](/wiki/Athlone,_Cape_Town "Athlone, Cape Town"), the *[Atlantic Sun](/wiki/Atlantic_Sun "Atlantic Sun")* , the *Constantiaberg Bulletin* from [Constantiaberg](/wiki/Constantiaberg,_Cape_Town "Constantiaberg, Cape Town"), the *City Vision* from [Bellville](/wiki/Bellville,_Cape_Town "Bellville, Cape Town"), the *[False Bay Echo](/wiki/False_Bay_Echo "False Bay Echo")* from False Bay, the *[Helderberg Sun](/wiki/Helderberg_Sun "Helderberg Sun")* from [Helderberg](/wiki/Helderberg,_Cape_Town "Helderberg, Cape Town"), the *[Plainsman](/wiki/Plainsman_(South_Africa) "Plainsman (South Africa)")* from Michell's Plain, the *[Sentinel News](/wiki/Sentinel_News "Sentinel News")* from Hout Bay, the *[Southern Mail](/wiki/Southern_Mail_(newspaper) "Southern Mail (newspaper)")* from the Southern Peninsula, the *[Southern Suburbs Tatler](/wiki/Southern_Suburbs_Tatler "Southern Suburbs Tatler")* from the [Southern Suburbs](/wiki/Southern_Suburbs,_Cape_Town "Southern Suburbs, Cape Town"), *[Table Talk](/wiki/Table_Talk_(Cape_Town) "Table Talk (Cape Town)")* from Table View and *[Tygertalk](/wiki/Tygertalk "Tygertalk")* from Tygervalley/Durbanville. Afrikaans language community newspapers include the *[Landbou-Burger](/wiki/Landbou-Burger "Landbou-Burger")* and the *[Tygerburger](/wiki/Tygerburger "Tygerburger")* . *[Vukani](/wiki/Vukani "Vukani")* , based in the Cape Flats, is published in [Xhosa](/wiki/Xhosa_language "Xhosa language").^[\[248\]](#cite_note-249)^{#cite_ref-249}

Cape Town is a centre for major broadcast media with several radio stations that only broadcast within the city. [94.5 Kfm](/wiki/KFM_(Cape_Town) "KFM (Cape Town)") (94.5 [MHz](/wiki/MHz "MHz") FM) and [Good Hope FM](/wiki/Good_Hope_FM "Good Hope FM") (94--97 MHz [FM](/wiki/FM_broadcasting "FM broadcasting")) mostly play [pop music](/wiki/Pop_music "Pop music"). Heart FM (104.9 MHz FM), the former P4 Radio, plays [jazz](/wiki/Jazz "Jazz") and [R\&B](/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B "Contemporary R&B"), while [Fine Music Radio](/wiki/Fine_Music_Radio "Fine Music Radio") (101.3 FM) plays [classical music](/wiki/European_classical_music "European classical music") and jazz, and Magic Music Radio^[\[249\]](#cite_note-250)^ (828 [kHz](/wiki/Kilohertz "Kilohertz") MW) plays adult contemporary and classic rock from the '80s, '90s and '00s.^[\[250\]](#cite_note-251)^ [Bush Radio](/wiki/Bush_Radio_(South_Africa) "Bush Radio (South Africa)") is a community radio station (89.5 MHz FM). The [Voice of the Cape](/wiki/Voice_of_the_Cape "Voice of the Cape") (95.8 MHz FM) and [Cape Talk](/wiki/Cape_Talk "Cape Talk") (567 kHz [MW](/wiki/Mediumwave "Mediumwave")) are the major [talk radio stations](/wiki/Talk_radio "Talk radio") in the city.^[\[251\]](#cite_note-252)^ Bokradio (98.9 MHz FM) is an Afrikaans music station.^[\[252\]](#cite_note-253)^ The [University of Cape Town](/wiki/University_of_Cape_Town "University of Cape Town") also runs its own radio station, [UCT Radio](/wiki/UCT_Radio "UCT Radio") (104.5 MHz FM).{#cite_ref-253}

The [SABC](/wiki/SABC "SABC") has a small presence in the city, with satellite studios located at [Sea Point](/wiki/Sea_Point "Sea Point"). [e.tv](/wiki/E.tv "E.tv") has a greater presence, with a large complex located at Longkloof Studios in [Gardens](/wiki/Gardens,_Cape_Town "Gardens, Cape Town"). [M-Net](/wiki/M-Net "M-Net") is not well represented with infrastructure within the city. [Cape Town TV](/wiki/Cape_Town_TV "Cape Town TV") is a local TV station, supported by numerous organisation and focusing mostly on documentaries. Numerous productions companies and their support industries are located in the city, mostly supporting the production of overseas commercials, model shoots, TV-series and movies.^[\[253\]](#cite_note-254)^ The local media infrastructure remains primarily in Johannesburg.{#cite_ref-254}  

### Sport and recreation {#Sport_and_recreation}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Cape_Town&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Sport and recreation")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/New_stadium_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-New_stadium_-_panoramio.jpg)](/wiki/File:New_stadium_-_panoramio.jpg) [Cape Town Stadium](/wiki/Cape_Town_Stadium "Cape Town Stadium") in [Green Point](/wiki/Green_Point,_Cape_Town "Green Point, Cape Town") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Newlands2.jpg/220px-Newlands2.jpg)](/wiki/File:Newlands2.jpg) [Newlands Cricket Ground](/wiki/Newlands_Cricket_Ground "Newlands Cricket Ground") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Newlands_stadium_cropped.jpg/220px-Newlands_stadium_cropped.jpg)](/wiki/File:Newlands_stadium_cropped.jpg) [Newlands Stadium](/wiki/Newlands_Stadium "Newlands Stadium") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Kitesurfers-001.JPG/220px-Kitesurfers-001.JPG)](/wiki/File:Kitesurfers-001.JPG) [Kitesurfing](/wiki/Kitesurfing "Kitesurfing") in [Table Bay](/wiki/Table_Bay "Table Bay")

Cape Town's most popular sports by participation are [cricket](/wiki/Cricket "Cricket"), [association football](/wiki/Association_football "Association football"), [swimming](/wiki/Swimming_(sport) "Swimming (sport)"), and [rugby union](/wiki/Rugby_union "Rugby union").^[\[254\]](#cite_note-255)^ In rugby union, Cape Town is the home of the [Western Province](/wiki/Western_Province_(rugby) "Western Province (rugby)") side, who play at [Cape Town Stadium](/wiki/Cape_Town_Stadium "Cape Town Stadium") and compete in the [Currie Cup](/wiki/Currie_Cup "Currie Cup"). In addition, Western Province players (along with some from Wellington's [Boland Cavaliers](/wiki/Boland_Cavaliers "Boland Cavaliers")) comprise the [Stormers](/wiki/Stormers "Stormers") in the [United Rugby Championship](/wiki/United_Rugby_Championship "United Rugby Championship") competition. Cape Town has also been a host city for both the [1995 Rugby World Cup](/wiki/1995_Rugby_World_Cup "1995 Rugby World Cup") and [2010 FIFA World Cup](/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup "2010 FIFA World Cup"), and annually hosts the Africa leg of the [World Rugby 7s](/wiki/World_Rugby_Sevens_Series "World Rugby Sevens Series").^[\[255\]](#cite_note-256)^ It has hosted the [2023 Netball World Cup](/wiki/2023_Netball_World_Cup "2023 Netball World Cup").^[\[256\]](#cite_note-257)^{#cite_ref-257}

[Association football](/wiki/Association_football "Association football"), which is mostly known as *soccer* in South Africa, is also popular. One [club](/wiki/Football_club_(association_football) "Football club (association football)") from Cape Town plays in the [Premiership](/wiki/South_African_Premiership "South African Premiership"), South Africa's premier league, [Cape Town City F.C.](/wiki/Cape_Town_City_F.C._(2016) "Cape Town City F.C. (2016)") Cape Town was also the location of several of the matches of the [2010 FIFA World Cup](/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup "2010 FIFA World Cup") including a semi-final,^[\[257\]](#cite_note-southafrica.info-258)^ held in South Africa. The Mother City built a new 70,000-seat stadium ([Cape Town Stadium](/wiki/Cape_Town_Stadium "Cape Town Stadium")) in the Green Point area.{#cite_ref-southafrica.info_258-0}

In [cricket](/wiki/Cricket "Cricket"), the [Cape Cobras](/wiki/Cape_Cobras "Cape Cobras") represent Cape Town at the [Newlands Cricket Ground](/wiki/Newlands_Cricket_Ground "Newlands Cricket Ground"). The team is the result of an amalgamation of the [Western Province Cricket](/wiki/Western_Province_Cricket "Western Province Cricket") and [Boland Cricket](/wiki/Boland_Cricket "Boland Cricket") teams. They take part in the [Supersport](/wiki/Supersport_Series "Supersport Series") and [Standard Bank Cup Series](/wiki/Standard_Bank_Cup_Series "Standard Bank Cup Series"). The Newlands Cricket Ground regularly hosts international matches.

Cape Town has had Olympic aspirations. For example, in 1996, Cape Town was one of the five candidate cities shortlisted by the [IOC](/wiki/IOC "IOC") to launch official candidatures to host the [2004 Summer Olympics](/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics "2004 Summer Olympics"). Although the Games ultimately went to [Athens](/wiki/Athens "Athens"), Cape Town came in third place. There has been some speculation that Cape Town was seeking the South African Olympic Committee's nomination to be South Africa's bid city for the [2020 Summer Olympic Games](/wiki/2020_Summer_Olympic_Games "2020 Summer Olympic Games").^[\[258\]](#cite_note-259)^ That was quashed when the [International Olympic Committee](/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee "International Olympic Committee") awarded the 2020 Games to Tokyo.{#cite_ref-259}

The city of Cape Town has vast experience in hosting major national and international sports events. The [Cape Town Cycle Tour](/wiki/Cape_Town_Cycle_Tour "Cape Town Cycle Tour") is the world's largest individually timed [road cycling race](/wiki/Road_bicycle_racing "Road bicycle racing") -- and the first event outside Europe to be included in the [International Cycling Union's Golden Bike series](/wiki/UCI_Golden_Bike "UCI Golden Bike"). It sees over 35,000 cyclists tackling a 109 km (68 mi) route around Cape Town. The [Absa Cape Epic](/wiki/Absa_Cape_Epic "Absa Cape Epic") is the largest full-service mountain bike stage race in the world. Some notable events hosted by Cape Town have included the [1995 Rugby World Cup](/wiki/1995_Rugby_World_Cup "1995 Rugby World Cup"), [2003 ICC Cricket World Cup](/wiki/2003_ICC_Cricket_World_Cup "2003 ICC Cricket World Cup"), and World Championships in various sports such as athletics, fencing, weightlifting, hockey, cycling, canoeing, gymnastics and others.

Cape Town was also a host city to the [2010 FIFA World Cup](/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup "2010 FIFA World Cup") from 11 June to 11 July 2010, further enhancing its profile as a major events city. It was also one of the host cities of the [2009 Indian Premier League](/wiki/2009_Indian_Premier_League "2009 Indian Premier League") cricket tournament. The Mother City has also played host to the [Africa leg](/wiki/South_Africa_Sevens "South Africa Sevens") of the annual [World Rugby 7s](/wiki/World_Rugby_Sevens_Series "World Rugby Sevens Series") event since 2015; for nine seasons, from 2002 until 2010, the event was staged in [George](/wiki/George,_Western_Cape "George, Western Cape") in the Western Cape, before moving to [Port Elizabeth](/wiki/Port_Elizabeth "Port Elizabeth") for the [2011 edition](/wiki/2011_South_Africa_Sevens "2011 South Africa Sevens"), and then to Cape Town in 2015. The event usually takes place in mid-December, and is hosted at the [Cape Town Stadium](/wiki/Cape_Town_Stadium "Cape Town Stadium") in Green Point.^[\[259\]](#cite_note-260)^{#cite_ref-260}

There are several golf courses in Cape Town. The Clovelly Country Club and Metropolitan Golf Club have 18 holes.^[\[260\]](#cite_note-261)^{#cite_ref-261}

The coastline of Cape Town is relatively long, and the varied exposure to weather conditions makes it fairly common for water conditions to be conducive to recreational scuba diving at some part of the city's coast. There is considerable variation in the underwater environment and regional ecology as there are dive sites on reefs and wrecks on both sides of the Cape Peninsula and False Bay, split between two coastal marine ecoregions by the Cape Peninsula, and also variable by depth zone.
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Blue_Wall_of_Sandy_Bay.jpg/220px-Blue_Wall_of_Sandy_Bay.jpg)](/wiki/File:Blue_Wall_of_Sandy_Bay.jpg) Surfing in [Sandy Bay](/wiki/Sandy_Bay,_Cape_Town "Sandy Bay, Cape Town")

False Bay is open to the south, and the prevailing open ocean swell arrives from the southwest, so the exposure varies considerably around the coastline. The inshore bathymetry near Cape Point is shallow enough for a moderate amount of refraction of long period swell, but deep enough to have less effect on short period swell, and acts as a filter to pass mainly the longer swell components to the Western shores, although they are significantly attenuated.

The eastern shores get more of the open ocean spectrum, and this results in very different swell conditions between the two sides at any given time. The fetch is generally too short for southeasterly winds to produce good surf. There are more than 20 [named breaks in False Bay](/wiki/False_Bay#Surfing "False Bay"). The north-wester can have a long fetch and can produce large waves, but they may also be associated with local wind and be very poorly sorted. The Atlantic coast is exposed to the full power of the South-westerly swell produced by the westerly winds of the southern ocean, often a long way away, so the swell has time to separate into similar wavelengths, and there are some world class big wave breaks among the named breaks of the Atlantic shore.^[\[261\]](#cite_note-Wavescape_1-262)^^[\[262\]](#cite_note-Wavescape_2-263)^^[\[263\]](#cite_note-Wavescape_3-264)^{#cite_ref-Wavescape_3_264-0}  
Further information on the racing sailboat built in Cape Town: [Cape 31](/wiki/Cape_31 "Cape 31")

In the 1950s the city was part of four editions of the famous [Algiers-Cape Town Rally](/wiki/Algiers-Cape_Town_Rally "Algiers-Cape Town Rally"), during the pioneer years of trans-Africa rallying and motor exploration. The closing of the road to the newly founded [Zaire](/wiki/Zaire "Zaire") caused the city to be dropped from the traject.^[\[264\]](#cite_note-265)^{#cite_ref-265}
